<p><b>Virginia</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="'v' in 'vie'">v</span><span title="/ər/: 'er' in 'letter'">ər</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="/dʒ/: 'j' in 'jam'">dʒ</span><span title="/ɪ/: 'i' in 'kit'">ɪ</span><span title="'n' in 'nigh'">n</span><span title="/j/: 'y' in 'yes'">j</span><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span></span>/</a></span><small class="nowrap metadata"> (<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:En-us-Virginia.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/></a> </span><a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/5/51/En-us-Virginia.ogg" title="En-us-Virginia.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</small></span>, <span class="nowrap"><small><a href="/wiki/British_English" title="British English">UK</a>:</small> <span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="'v' in 'vie'">v</span><span title="/ər/: 'er' in 'letter'">ər</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="/dʒ/: 'j' in 'jam'">dʒ</span><span title="/ɪ/: 'i' in 'kit'">ɪ</span><span title="'n' in 'nigh'">n</span><span title="/iː/ or /ɪ/: 'y' in 'happy'">i</span><span title="/./: syllable break">.</span><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span></span>/</a></span></span>, officially the <b>Commonwealth of Virginia</b>) is a state in the <a href="/wiki/Southeastern_United_States" title="Southeastern United States">Southeastern</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> and Mid-Atlantic<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> regions of the United States located between the <a href="/wiki/East_Coast_of_the_United_States" title="East Coast of the United States">Atlantic Coast</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Appalachian_Mountains" title="Appalachian Mountains">Appalachian Mountains</a>. Virginia is nicknamed the "Old Dominion" due to its status as the first English colonial possession established in mainland North America,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-encolddominion_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-encolddominion-8">[8]</a></sup> and "Mother of Presidents" because <a href="/wiki/List_of_Presidents_of_the_United_States_by_home_state#Places_of_birth" title="List of Presidents of the United States by home state">eight U.S. presidents</a> were born there, more than any other state. The geography and climate of the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_(U.S._state)" title="Commonwealth (U.S. state)">Commonwealth</a> are shaped by the <a href="/wiki/Blue_Ridge_Mountains" title="Blue Ridge Mountains">Blue Ridge Mountains</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Chesapeake_Bay" title="Chesapeake Bay">Chesapeake Bay</a>, which provide habitat for much of its flora and fauna. The capital of the Commonwealth is <a href="/wiki/Richmond,_Virginia" title="Richmond, Virginia">Richmond</a>; <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Beach,_Virginia" title="Virginia Beach, Virginia">Virginia Beach</a> is the most populous city, and <a href="/wiki/Fairfax_County,_Virginia" title="Fairfax County, Virginia">Fairfax County</a> is the most populous political subdivision. The Commonwealth's estimated population as of 2017<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Virginia&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> is over 8.4 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PopHousingEst_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-PopHousingEst-2">[2]</a></sup></p>
<p>The area's history begins with <a href="/wiki/Native_American_tribes_in_Virginia" title="Native American tribes in Virginia">several indigenous groups</a>, including the <a href="/wiki/Powhatan" title="Powhatan">Powhatan</a>. In 1607 the <a href="/wiki/London_Company" title="London Company">London Company</a> established the <a href="/wiki/Colony_of_Virginia" title="Colony of Virginia">Colony of Virginia</a> as the first permanent <a href="/wiki/New_World" title="New World">New World</a> <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_England" title="Kingdom of England">English</a> colony. Slave labor and the land acquired from displaced Native American tribes each played a significant role in the colony's early politics and plantation economy. Virginia was one of the <a href="/wiki/Thirteen_Colonies" title="Thirteen Colonies">13 Colonies</a> in the <a href="/wiki/American_Revolution" title="American Revolution">American Revolution</a> and joined the <a href="/wiki/Confederate_States_of_America" title="Confederate States of America">Confederacy</a> in the <a href="/wiki/American_Civil_War" title="American Civil War">American Civil War</a>, during which Richmond was made the Confederate capital and Virginia's northwestern counties <a href="/wiki/Wheeling_Convention" title="Wheeling Convention">seceded</a> to form the state of <a href="/wiki/West_Virginia" title="West Virginia">West Virginia</a>. Although the Commonwealth was under <a href="/wiki/Solid_South" title="Solid South">one-party rule</a> for nearly a century following <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Reconstruction_era_of_the_United_States" title="Reconstruction era of the United States">Reconstruction</a>, both major national parties are competitive in modern Virginia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-purple_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-purple-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Virginia_General_Assembly" title="Virginia General Assembly">Virginia General Assembly</a> is the oldest continuous law-making body in the New World.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> The state government was ranked most effective by the <a href="/wiki/Pew_Research_Center" title="Pew Research Center">Pew Center on the States</a> in both 2005 and 2008.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pew_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-pew-11">[11]</a></sup> It is unique in how it treats cities and counties equally, manages local roads, and prohibits its governors from serving consecutive terms. Virginia's economy has many sectors: agriculture in the <a href="/wiki/Shenandoah_Valley" title="Shenandoah Valley">Shenandoah Valley</a>; federal agencies in <a href="/wiki/Northern_Virginia" title="Northern Virginia">Northern Virginia</a>, including the headquarters of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Defense" title="United States Department of Defense">U.S. Department of Defense</a> and <a href="/wiki/Central_Intelligence_Agency" title="Central Intelligence Agency">Central Intelligence Agency (CIA)</a>; and military facilities in <a href="/wiki/Hampton_Roads" title="Hampton Roads">Hampton Roads</a>, the site of the <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Port_Authority" title="Virginia Port Authority">region's main seaport</a>.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Environment_of_Virginia" title="Environment of Virginia">Environment of Virginia</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:264px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Virginia_painted_relief.png"><img alt="Terrain map of Virginia divided with lines into five regions. The first region on the far left is small and only in the state's panhandle. The next is larger and covers most of the western part of the state. The next is a thin strip that covers only the mountains. The next is a wide area in the middle of the state. The left most is based on the rivers which diffuse the previous region." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="205" data-file-width="388" height="138" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Virginia_painted_relief.png/262px-Virginia_painted_relief.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/1/1c/Virginia_painted_relief.png 1.5x" width="262"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Virginia_painted_relief.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Geographically and geologically, Virginia is divided into five regions from east to west: <a href="/wiki/Tidewater_region" title="Tidewater region">Tidewater</a>, <a href="/wiki/Piedmont_region_of_Virginia" title="Piedmont region of Virginia">Piedmont</a>, <a href="/wiki/Blue_Ridge_Mountains" title="Blue Ridge Mountains">Blue Ridge Mountains</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ridge-and-Valley_Appalachians" title="Ridge-and-Valley Appalachians">Ridge and Valley</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Cumberland_Plateau" title="Cumberland Plateau">Cumberland Plateau</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-eov_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-eov-12">[12]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Virginia has a total area of 42,774.2 square miles (110,784.7 km<sup>2</sup>), including 3,180.13 square miles (8,236.5 km<sup>2</sup>) of water, making it the 35th-<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._states_by_area" title="List of U.S. states by area">largest state</a> by area.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> Virginia is bordered by <a href="/wiki/Maryland" title="Maryland">Maryland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Washington,_D.C." title="Washington, D.C.">Washington, D.C.</a> to the north and east; by the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic Ocean</a> to the east; by <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina" title="North Carolina">North Carolina</a> to the south; by <a href="/wiki/Tennessee" title="Tennessee">Tennessee</a> to the southwest; by <a href="/wiki/Kentucky" title="Kentucky">Kentucky</a> to the west; and by <a href="/wiki/West_Virginia" title="West Virginia">West Virginia</a> to the north and west. Virginia's boundary with Maryland and Washington, D.C. extends to the low-water mark of the south shore of the <a href="/wiki/Potomac_River" title="Potomac River">Potomac River</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> The southern border is defined as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/36%C2%B030%27_parallel_north" title="36°30' parallel north">36° 30′ parallel north</a>, though surveyor error led to deviations of as much as three <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arcminute" title="Arcminute">arcminutes</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHubbard.2C_Jr.2009140_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHubbard.2C_Jr.2009140-15">[15]</a></sup> The border with Tennessee was not settled until 1893, when <a href="/wiki/Virginia_v._Tennessee" title="Virginia v. Tennessee">their dispute</a> was brought to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Supreme_Court" title="U.S. Supreme Court">U.S. Supreme Court</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVan_Zandt197692.E2.80.9395_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVan_Zandt197692.E2.80.9395-16">[16]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Geology_and_terrain">Geology and terrain</span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Chesapeake_Bay" title="Chesapeake Bay">Chesapeake Bay</a> separates the contiguous portion of the Commonwealth from the two-county peninsula of Virginia's <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Shore_of_Virginia" title="Eastern Shore of Virginia">Eastern Shore</a>. The bay was formed from the drowned river valleys of the <a href="/wiki/Susquehanna_River" title="Susquehanna River">Susquehanna River</a> and the <a href="/wiki/James_River" title="James River">James River</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bay_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-bay-17">[17]</a></sup> Many of <a href="/wiki/List_of_rivers_of_Virginia" title="List of rivers of Virginia">Virginia's rivers</a> flow into the Chesapeake Bay, including the <a href="/wiki/Potomac_River" title="Potomac River">Potomac</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rappahannock_River" title="Rappahannock River">Rappahannock</a>, <a href="/wiki/York_River_(Virginia)" title="York River (Virginia)">York</a>, and James, which create three peninsulas in the bay.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBurnhamBurnham20047.2C_56.E2.80.9357_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBurnhamBurnham20047.2C_56.E2.80.9357-18">[18]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Golden_Sunset_--Timber_Hollow_Overlook_(22014263936).jpg"><img alt="The rays of a sunset spread over mountain ridges that turn from green to purple and blue as they progress toward the horizon." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="5428" data-file-width="3573" height="258" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Golden_Sunset_--Timber_Hollow_Overlook_%2822014263936%29.jpg/170px-Golden_Sunset_--Timber_Hollow_Overlook_%2822014263936%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Golden_Sunset_--Timber_Hollow_Overlook_%2822014263936%29.jpg/255px-Golden_Sunset_--Timber_Hollow_Overlook_%2822014263936%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Golden_Sunset_--Timber_Hollow_Overlook_%2822014263936%29.jpg/340px-Golden_Sunset_--Timber_Hollow_Overlook_%2822014263936%29.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Golden_Sunset_--Timber_Hollow_Overlook_(22014263936).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Deciduous and evergreen trees give the <a href="/wiki/Blue_Ridge_Mountains" title="Blue Ridge Mountains">Blue Ridge Mountains</a> their distinct color.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHeinemannKolpParent.2C_Jr.Shade20073_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHeinemannKolpParent.2C_Jr.Shade20073-20">[20]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tidewater_(geographic_term)" title="Tidewater (geographic term)">Tidewater</a> is a <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_coastal_plain" title="Atlantic coastal plain">coastal plain</a> between the Atlantic coast and the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Seaboard_fall_line" title="Atlantic Seaboard fall line">fall line</a>. It includes the Eastern Shore and major <a href="/wiki/Estuary" title="Estuary">estuaries</a> of Chesapeake Bay. The Piedmont is a series of <a href="/wiki/Sedimentary_rock" title="Sedimentary rock">sedimentary</a> and <a href="/wiki/Igneous_rock" title="Igneous rock">igneous rock</a>-based <a href="/wiki/Foothills" title="Foothills">foothills</a> east of the mountains which were formed in the <a href="/wiki/Mesozoic" title="Mesozoic">Mesozoic</a> era.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPazzaglia2006135.E2.80.93138_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPazzaglia2006135.E2.80.93138-21">[21]</a></sup> The region, known for its heavy clay soil, includes the <a href="/wiki/Southwest_Mountains" title="Southwest Mountains">Southwest Mountains</a> around <a href="/wiki/Charlottesville,_Virginia" title="Charlottesville, Virginia">Charlottesville</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-agriculture_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-agriculture-22">[22]</a></sup> The Blue Ridge Mountains are a <a href="/wiki/Physiographic_regions_of_the_world" title="Physiographic regions of the world">physiographic province</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Appalachian_Mountains" title="Appalachian Mountains">Appalachian Mountains</a> with the highest points in the state, the tallest being <a href="/wiki/Mount_Rogers" title="Mount Rogers">Mount Rogers</a> at 5,729 feet (1,746 m).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBurnhamBurnham2004277_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBurnhamBurnham2004277-23">[23]</a></sup> The Ridge and Valley region is west of the mountains and includes the <a href="/wiki/Great_Appalachian_Valley" title="Great Appalachian Valley">Great Appalachian Valley</a>. The region is <a href="/wiki/Carbonate_rock" title="Carbonate rock">carbonate rock</a> based and includes <a href="/wiki/Massanutten_Mountain" title="Massanutten Mountain">Massanutten Mountain</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-regions_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-regions-24">[24]</a></sup> The Cumberland Plateau and the <a href="/wiki/Cumberland_Mountains" title="Cumberland Mountains">Cumberland Mountains</a> are in the southwest corner of Virginia, south of the <a href="/wiki/Allegheny_Plateau" title="Allegheny Plateau">Allegheny Plateau</a>. In this region, rivers flow northwest, with a <a href="/wiki/Drainage_system_(geomorphology)#Dendritic_drainage_pattern" title="Drainage system (geomorphology)">dendritic drainage system</a>, into the <a href="/wiki/Ohio_River" title="Ohio River">Ohio River</a> basin.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPalmer199849.E2.80.9351_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPalmer199849.E2.80.9351-25">[25]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Seismic_Zone" title="Virginia Seismic Zone">Virginia Seismic Zone</a> has not had a history of regular <a href="/wiki/Earthquake" title="Earthquake">earthquake</a> activity. Earthquakes are rarely above 4.5 in <a href="/wiki/Richter_magnitude_scale" title="Richter magnitude scale">magnitude</a>, because Virginia is located away from the edges of the <a href="/wiki/North_American_Plate" title="North American Plate">North American Plate</a>. The largest earthquake, at an estimated 5.9 magnitude, was in 1897 near <a href="/wiki/Blacksburg,_Virginia" title="Blacksburg, Virginia">Blacksburg</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> A <a href="/wiki/2011_Virginia_earthquake" title="2011 Virginia earthquake">5.8 magnitude earthquake</a> struck central Virginia on August 23, 2011, near <a href="/wiki/Mineral,_Virginia" title="Mineral, Virginia">Mineral</a>. The earthquake was reportedly felt as far away as <a href="/wiki/Toronto" title="Toronto">Toronto</a>, <a href="/wiki/Atlanta" title="Atlanta">Atlanta</a> and <a href="/wiki/Florida" title="Florida">Florida</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Coal_mining_in_the_United_States" title="Coal mining in the United States">Coal mining</a> takes place in the three mountainous regions at 45 distinct coal beds near Mesozoic basins.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mining_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-mining-28">[28]</a></sup> Over 62 million tons of other non-fuel resources, such as <a href="/wiki/Slate" title="Slate">slate</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kyanite" title="Kyanite">kyanite</a>, sand, or gravel, were also mined in Virginia in 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> The state's carbonate rock is filled with more than 4,000 caves, ten of which are open for tourism.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> 35 million years ago, a <a href="/wiki/Bolide" title="Bolide">bolide</a> impacted what is now eastern Virginia. The <a href="/wiki/Chesapeake_Bay_impact_crater" title="Chesapeake Bay impact crater">resulting crater</a> may explain <a href="/wiki/Subsidence" title="Subsidence">sinking</a> and <a href="/wiki/Earthquake" title="Earthquake">earthquakes</a> in the region.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup></p>

<td colspan="12" style="padding: 2px; text-align: left; line-height: 1.5em; color: red">Average max. and min. temperatures in °C</td>

<td colspan="12" style="padding: 2px; text-align: left; line-height: 1.5em; color: blue">Precipitation totals in mm</td>

<p>The climate of Virginia is <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Humid_subtropical" title="Humid subtropical">humid subtropical</a> and becomes increasingly warmer and more humid farther south and east.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Burnham_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-Burnham-32">[32]</a></sup> Seasonal extremes vary from average lows of 26 °F (−3 °C) in January to average highs of 86 °F (30 °C) in July. The Atlantic Ocean has a strong effect on eastern and southeastern coastal areas of the state. Influenced by the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_Stream" title="Gulf Stream">Gulf Stream</a>, coastal weather is subject to <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone" title="Tropical cyclone">hurricanes</a>, most pronouncedly near the mouth of Chesapeake Bay.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-climatology_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-climatology-33">[33]</a></sup> In spite of its position adjacent to the Atlantic Ocean, even the coastal areas have a significant continental influence with quite large temperature differences between summer and winter, particularly given the state climate's subtropical classification, which is typical of states in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Upper_South" title="Upper South">Upper South</a>.</p>
<p>Virginia has an annual average of 35–45 days of thunderstorm activity, particularly in the western part of the state,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tstorms_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-tstorms-34">[34]</a></sup> and an average annual precipitation of 42.7 inches (108 cm).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-climatology_33-1"><a href="#cite_note-climatology-33">[33]</a></sup> Cold air masses arriving over the mountains in winter can lead to significant snowfalls, such as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Blizzard_of_1996" title="Blizzard of 1996">Blizzard of 1996</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Winter_storms_of_2009%E2%80%932010" title="Winter storms of 2009–2010">winter storms of 2009–2010</a>. The interaction of these elements with the state's topography creates distinct <a href="/wiki/Microclimate" title="Microclimate">microclimates</a> in the Shenandoah Valley, the mountainous southwest, and the coastal plains.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> Virginia averages seven <a href="/wiki/Tornado" title="Tornado">tornadoes</a> annually, most F2 or lower on the <a href="/wiki/Fujita_scale" title="Fujita scale">Fujita scale</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup></p>
<p>In recent years, the expansion of the southern suburbs of <a href="/wiki/Washington,_D.C." title="Washington, D.C.">Washington, D.C.</a> into <a href="/wiki/Northern_Virginia" title="Northern Virginia">Northern Virginia</a> has introduced an <a href="/wiki/Urban_heat_island" title="Urban heat island">urban heat island</a> primarily caused by increased absorption of solar radiation in more densely populated areas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> In the <a href="/wiki/American_Lung_Association" title="American Lung Association">American Lung Association</a>'s 2011 report, 11 counties received failing grades for air quality, with <a href="/wiki/Fairfax_County,_Virginia" title="Fairfax County, Virginia">Fairfax County</a> having the worst in the state, due to automobile pollution.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-polution_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-polution-38">[38]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> Haze in the mountains is caused in part by coal power plants.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ecosystem">Ecosystem</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_endangered_species_in_Virginia" title="List of endangered species in Virginia">List of endangered species in Virginia</a></div>
<p>Forests cover 65% of the state, primarily with deciduous, broad leaf trees in the western part of the state and evergreens and conifers dominant the central and eastern part of Virginia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-forests_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-forests-41">[41]</a></sup> Lower altitudes are more likely to have small but dense stands of moisture-loving hemlocks and mosses in abundance, with hickory and oak in the Blue Ridge.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Burnham_32-1"><a href="#cite_note-Burnham-32">[32]</a></sup> However, since the early 1990s, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gypsy_moth" title="Gypsy moth">Gypsy moth</a> infestations have eroded the dominance of oak forests.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> In the lowland tidewater and piedmont, yellow pines tend to dominate, with bald cypress wetland forests in the Great Dismal and Nottoway swamps. Other common trees and plants include red bay, wax myrtle, dwarf palmetto, <a href="/wiki/Liriodendron_tulipifera" title="Liriodendron tulipifera">tulip poplar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kalmia_latifolia" title="Kalmia latifolia">mountain laurel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Asclepias" title="Asclepias">milkweed</a>, daisies, and many species of ferns. The largest areas of wilderness are along the Atlantic coast and in the western mountains, where the largest populations of <a href="/wiki/Trillium_grandiflorum" title="Trillium grandiflorum">trillium wildflowers</a> in North America are found.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Burnham_32-2"><a href="#cite_note-Burnham-32">[32]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECarrollMiller2002xi.E2.88.92xii_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECarrollMiller2002xi.E2.88.92xii-43">[43]</a></sup> The Atlantic coast regions are host to flora commonly associated with the South Atlantic pine forests and lower Southeast Coastal Plain maritime flora, the latter found primarily in eastern and central Virginia.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Deer_Big_Meadow_(13082497565).jpg"><img alt="Two red-brown colored deer graze among tall grass and purple flowers in a meadow." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3000" data-file-width="3000" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Deer_Big_Meadow_%2813082497565%29.jpg/220px-Deer_Big_Meadow_%2813082497565%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Deer_Big_Meadow_%2813082497565%29.jpg/330px-Deer_Big_Meadow_%2813082497565%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Deer_Big_Meadow_%2813082497565%29.jpg/440px-Deer_Big_Meadow_%2813082497565%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Deer_Big_Meadow_(13082497565).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
White-tailed deer, also known as Virginia deer, graze at <a href="/wiki/Big_Meadows" title="Big Meadows">Big Meadows</a> in <a href="/wiki/Shenandoah_National_Park" title="Shenandoah National Park">Shenandoah National Park</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Mammals include <a href="/wiki/White-tailed_deer" title="White-tailed deer">white-tailed deer</a>, <a href="/wiki/American_black_bear" title="American black bear">black bear</a>, <a href="/wiki/Beaver" title="Beaver">beaver</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bobcat" title="Bobcat">bobcat</a>, <a href="/wiki/Coyote" title="Coyote">coyote</a>, <a href="/wiki/Raccoon" title="Raccoon">raccoon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Skunk" title="Skunk">skunk</a>, <a href="/wiki/Groundhog" title="Groundhog">groundhog</a>, <a href="/wiki/Virginia_opossum" title="Virginia opossum">Virginia opossum</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gray_fox" title="Gray fox">gray fox</a>, <a href="/wiki/Red_fox" title="Red fox">red fox</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eastern_cottontail_rabbit" title="Eastern cottontail rabbit">eastern cottontail rabbit</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> Other mammals include: nutria, fox squirrel, gray squirrel, flying squirrel, chipmunk, brown bat, and weasel. Birds include <a href="/wiki/Northern_cardinal" title="Northern cardinal">cardinals</a> (the state bird), barred owls, Carolina chickadees, red-tailed hawks, ospreys, brown pelicans, quail, seagulls, bald eagles, and wild turkeys. Virginia is also home to the pileated woodpecker as well as the red-bellied woodpecker. The <a href="/wiki/Peregrine_falcon" title="Peregrine falcon">peregrine falcon</a> was reintroduced into Shenandoah National Park in the mid-1990s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> Walleye, brook trout, Roanoke bass, and blue catfish are among the 210 known species of freshwater fish.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> Running brooks with rocky bottoms are often inhabited by plentiful amounts of crayfish and salamanders.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Burnham_32-3"><a href="#cite_note-Burnham-32">[32]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Chesapeake_Bay" title="Chesapeake Bay">Chesapeake Bay</a> is host to many species, including <a href="/wiki/Callinectes_sapidus" title="Callinectes sapidus">blue crabs</a>, clams, oysters, and rockfish (also known as striped bass).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup></p>
<p>Virginia has 30 <a href="/wiki/National_Park_Service" title="National Park Service">National Park Service</a> units, such as <a href="/wiki/Great_Falls_Park" title="Great Falls Park">Great Falls Park</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Appalachian_Trail" title="Appalachian Trail">Appalachian Trail</a>, and one national park, the <a href="/wiki/Shenandoah_National_Park" title="Shenandoah National Park">Shenandoah National Park</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> Shenandoah was established in 1935 and encompasses the scenic <a href="/wiki/Skyline_Drive" title="Skyline Drive">Skyline Drive</a>. Almost 40% of the park's area (79,579 acres/322 km<sup>2</sup>) has been designated as wilderness under the <a href="/wiki/National_Wilderness_Preservation_System" title="National Wilderness Preservation System">National Wilderness Preservation System</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECarrollMiller2002158_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECarrollMiller2002158-49">[49]</a></sup> Additionally, there are 34 <a href="/wiki/List_of_Virginia_state_parks" title="List of Virginia state parks">Virginia state parks</a> and 17 <a href="/wiki/List_of_Virginia_state_forests" title="List of Virginia state forests">state forests</a>, run by the Department of Conservation and Recreation and the Department of Forestry.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-forests_41-1"><a href="#cite_note-forests-41">[41]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> The Chesapeake Bay, while not a national park, is protected by both state and federal legislation, and the jointly run <a href="/wiki/Chesapeake_Bay_Program" title="Chesapeake Bay Program">Chesapeake Bay Program</a> which conducts restoration on the bay and its watershed. The <a href="/wiki/Great_Dismal_Swamp_National_Wildlife_Refuge" title="Great Dismal Swamp National Wildlife Refuge">Great Dismal Swamp National Wildlife Refuge</a> extends into North Carolina, as does the <a href="/wiki/Back_Bay_National_Wildlife_Refuge" title="Back Bay National Wildlife Refuge">Back Bay National Wildlife Refuge</a>, which marks the beginning of the <a href="/wiki/Outer_Banks" title="Outer Banks">Outer Banks</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith2008152.E2.80.93153.2C_356_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith2008152.E2.80.93153.2C_356-51">[51]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Virginia" title="History of Virginia">History of Virginia</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:John_Smith_Saved_by_Pocahontas.jpg"><img alt="A painting of a young dark-haired Native American woman shielding an Elizabethan era man from execution by a Native American chief. She is bare-chested, and her face is bathed in light from an unknown source. Several Native Americans look on at the scene." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="971" data-file-width="750" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/John_Smith_Saved_by_Pocahontas.jpg/170px-John_Smith_Saved_by_Pocahontas.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/John_Smith_Saved_by_Pocahontas.jpg/255px-John_Smith_Saved_by_Pocahontas.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/John_Smith_Saved_by_Pocahontas.jpg/340px-John_Smith_Saved_by_Pocahontas.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:John_Smith_Saved_by_Pocahontas.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The story of <a href="/wiki/Pocahontas" title="Pocahontas">Pocahontas</a>, an ancestress of many of the <a href="/wiki/First_Families_of_Virginia" title="First Families of Virginia">First Families of Virginia</a>, was romanticized by later artists.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>"Jamestown 2007" marked Virginia's quadricentennial year, celebrating 400 years since the establishment of the Jamestown Colony. The celebrations highlighted contributions from <a href="/wiki/Native_Americans_in_the_United_States" title="Native Americans in the United States">Native Americans</a>, Africans, and Europeans, each of which had a significant part in shaping Virginia's history.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWallenstein2007406.E2.80.93407_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWallenstein2007406.E2.80.93407-53">[53]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> Warfare, including among these groups, has also had an important role. Virginia was a focal point in conflicts from the <a href="/wiki/French_and_Indian_War" title="French and Indian War">French and Indian War</a>, the <a href="/wiki/American_Revolution" title="American Revolution">American Revolution</a> and the <a href="/wiki/American_Civil_War" title="American Civil War">Civil War</a>, to the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/War_on_Terrorism" title="War on Terrorism">War on Terrorism</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> Stories about historic figures, such as those surrounding <a href="/wiki/Pocahontas" title="Pocahontas">Pocahontas</a> and <a href="/wiki/John_Smith_(explorer)" title="John Smith (explorer)">John Smith</a>, <a href="/wiki/George_Washington" title="George Washington">George Washington</a>'s childhood, or the plantation elite in the slave society of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Antebellum_Era_in_the_United_States" title="Antebellum Era in the United States">antebellum period</a>, have also created potent myths of state history, and have served as rationales for Virginia's ideology.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAbrams1999xv_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAbrams1999xv-56">[56]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Colony">Colony</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Colony_of_Virginia" title="Colony of Virginia">Colony of Virginia</a></div>
<p>The first people are estimated to have arrived in Virginia over 12,000 years ago.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> By 5,000 years ago more permanent settlements emerged, and farming began by 900 AD. By 1500, the <a href="/wiki/Algonquian_peoples" title="Algonquian peoples">Algonquian peoples</a> had founded towns such as <a href="/wiki/Werowocomoco" title="Werowocomoco">Werowocomoco</a> in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tidewater_region_of_Virginia" title="Tidewater region of Virginia">Tidewater region</a>, which they referred to as <i><a href="/wiki/Tsenacommacah" title="Tsenacommacah">Tsenacommacah</a></i>. The other major language groups in the area were the <a href="/wiki/Siouan_languages" title="Siouan languages">Siouan</a> to the west, and the <a href="/wiki/Iroquoian_languages" title="Iroquoian languages">Iroquoians</a>, who included the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nottoway_Tribe" title="Nottoway Tribe">Nottoway</a> and <a href="/wiki/Meherrin" title="Meherrin">Meherrin</a>, to the north and south. After 1570, the Algonquians consolidated under <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chief_Powhatan" title="Chief Powhatan">Chief Powhatan</a> in response to threats from these other groups on their trade network.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHeinemannKolpParent.2C_Jr.Shade20074.E2.80.9311_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHeinemannKolpParent.2C_Jr.Shade20074.E2.80.9311-58">[58]</a></sup> Powhatan controlled more than 30 smaller tribes and over 150 settlements, who shared a common <a href="/wiki/Powhatan_language" title="Powhatan language">Virginia Algonquian</a> language. In 1607, the native Tidewater population was between 13,000 and 14,000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup></p>
<p>Several European expeditions, including a <a href="/wiki/Ajac%C3%A1n_Mission" title="Ajacán Mission">group of Spanish Jesuits</a>, explored the <a href="/wiki/Chesapeake_Bay" title="Chesapeake Bay">Chesapeake Bay</a> during the 16th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> In 1583, Queen <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_I_of_England" title="Elizabeth I of England">Elizabeth I of England</a> granted <a href="/wiki/Walter_Raleigh" title="Walter Raleigh">Walter Raleigh</a> a charter to plant a colony north of <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Florida" title="Spanish Florida">Spanish Florida</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWallenstein20078.E2.80.939_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWallenstein20078.E2.80.939-61">[61]</a></sup> In 1584, Raleigh sent an expedition to the <a href="/wiki/East_Coast_of_the_United_States" title="East Coast of the United States">Atlantic coast of North America</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMoran20078_62-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMoran20078-62">[62]</a></sup> The name "Virginia" may have been suggested then by Raleigh or Elizabeth, perhaps noting her status as the "Virgin Queen," and may also be related to a native phrase, "Wingandacoa," or name, "Wingina."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStewart200822_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStewart200822-63">[63]</a></sup> Initially the name applied to the entire coastal region from South Carolina to Maine, plus the island of <a href="/wiki/Bermuda" title="Bermuda">Bermuda</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVollmann2002695.E2.80.93696_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVollmann2002695.E2.80.93696-64">[64]</a></sup> Later, subsequent royal charters modified the Colony's boundaries. The <a href="/wiki/London_Company" title="London Company">London Company</a> was incorporated as a joint stock company by the proprietary <a href="/wiki/Charter_of_1606" title="Charter of 1606">Charter of 1606</a>, which granted land rights to this area. The company financed the first permanent English settlement in the "<a href="/wiki/New_World" title="New World">New World</a>", <a href="/wiki/Jamestown,_Virginia" title="Jamestown, Virginia">Jamestown</a>. Named for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/James_I_of_England" title="James I of England">King James I</a>, it was founded in May 1607 by <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Newport" title="Christopher Newport">Christopher Newport</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEConlin200930.E2.80.9331_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEConlin200930.E2.80.9331-65">[65]</a></sup> In 1619, colonists took greater control with an elected legislature called the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Burgesses" title="House of Burgesses">House of Burgesses</a>. With the bankruptcy of the London Company in 1624, the settlement was taken into royal authority as an English <a href="/wiki/Crown_colony" title="Crown colony">crown colony</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGordon200417_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGordon200417-66">[66]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_Governor%27s_Palace_--_Williamsburg_(VA)_September_2012.jpg"><img alt="A three-story red brick colonial style hall and its left and right wings during summer." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1572" data-file-width="2565" height="135" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/The_Governor%27s_Palace_--_Williamsburg_%28VA%29_September_2012.jpg/220px-The_Governor%27s_Palace_--_Williamsburg_%28VA%29_September_2012.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/The_Governor%27s_Palace_--_Williamsburg_%28VA%29_September_2012.jpg/330px-The_Governor%27s_Palace_--_Williamsburg_%28VA%29_September_2012.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/The_Governor%27s_Palace_--_Williamsburg_%28VA%29_September_2012.jpg/440px-The_Governor%27s_Palace_--_Williamsburg_%28VA%29_September_2012.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:The_Governor%27s_Palace_--_Williamsburg_(VA)_September_2012.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Williamsburg,_Virginia" title="Williamsburg, Virginia">Williamsburg</a> was Virginia's capital from 1699 to 1780.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Life in the colony was perilous, and many died during the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Starving_Time_(Jamestown)" title="Starving Time (Jamestown)">Starving Time</a> in 1609 and the <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Powhatan_Wars" title="Anglo-Powhatan Wars">Anglo-Powhatan Wars</a>, including the <a href="/wiki/Indian_massacre_of_1622" title="Indian massacre of 1622">Indian massacre of 1622</a>, which fostered the colonists' negative view of all tribes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> By 1624, only 3,400 of the 6,000 early settlers had survived.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> However, European <a href="/wiki/Tobacco_in_the_American_Colonies" title="Tobacco in the American Colonies">demand for tobacco</a> fueled the arrival of more settlers and servants.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWallenstein200722_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWallenstein200722-69">[69]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Headright" title="Headright">headright</a> system tried to solve the labor shortage by providing colonists with land for each <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indentured_servant" title="Indentured servant">indentured servant</a> they transported to Virginia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHashaw200776.E2.80.9377.2C_239.E2.80.93240_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHashaw200776.E2.80.9377.2C_239.E2.80.93240-70">[70]</a></sup> African workers were first imported to Jamestown in 1619 initially under the rules of indentured servitude. The shift to a system of African <a href="/wiki/History_of_slavery_in_Virginia" title="History of slavery in Virginia">slavery in Virginia</a> was propelled by the legal cases of <a href="/wiki/John_Punch_(slave)" title="John Punch (slave)">John Punch</a>, who was sentenced to lifetime slavery in 1640 for attempting to run away,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> and of <a href="/wiki/John_Casor" title="John Casor">John Casor</a>, who was claimed by <a href="/wiki/Anthony_Johnson_(colonist)" title="Anthony Johnson (colonist)">Anthony Johnson</a> as his servant for life in 1655.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> Slavery first appears in Virginia statutes in 1661 and 1662, when a law made it hereditary based on the mother's status.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHashaw2007211.E2.80.93215_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHashaw2007211.E2.80.93215-73">[73]</a></sup></p>
<p>Tensions and the geographic differences between the working and ruling classes led to <a href="/wiki/Bacon%27s_Rebellion" title="Bacon's Rebellion">Bacon's Rebellion</a> in 1676, by which time current and former indentured servants made up as much as 80% of the population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHeinemannKolpParent.2C_Jr.Shade200751.E2.80.9359_74-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHeinemannKolpParent.2C_Jr.Shade200751.E2.80.9359-74">[74]</a></sup> Rebels, largely from the colony's frontier, were also opposed to the conciliatory policy towards <a href="/wiki/Native_American_tribes_in_Virginia" title="Native American tribes in Virginia">native tribes</a>, and one result of the rebellion was the signing at <a href="/wiki/Middle_Plantation_(Virginia)" title="Middle Plantation (Virginia)">Middle Plantation</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_1677" title="Treaty of 1677">Treaty of 1677</a>, which made the signatory tribes <a href="/wiki/Tributary_state" title="Tributary state">tributary states</a> and was part of a pattern of appropriating tribal land by force and treaty. Middle Plantation saw the founding of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_College_of_William_%26_Mary" title="The College of William &amp; Mary">The College of William &amp; Mary</a> in 1693 and was renamed <a href="/wiki/Williamsburg,_Virginia" title="Williamsburg, Virginia">Williamsburg</a> as it became the colonial capital in 1699.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHeinemannKolpParent.2C_Jr.Shade200776.E2.80.9377_75-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHeinemannKolpParent.2C_Jr.Shade200776.E2.80.9377-75">[75]</a></sup> In 1747, a group of Virginian speculators formed the <a href="/wiki/Ohio_Company" title="Ohio Company">Ohio Company</a>, with the backing of the British crown, to start English settlement and trade in the <a href="/wiki/Ohio_Country" title="Ohio Country">Ohio Country</a> west of the <a href="/wiki/Appalachian_Mountains" title="Appalachian Mountains">Appalachian Mountains</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAnderson200023_76-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAnderson200023-76">[76]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>, which claimed this area as part of their colony of <a href="/wiki/New_France" title="New France">New France</a>, viewed this as a threat, and the ensuing <a href="/wiki/French_and_Indian_War" title="French and Indian War">French and Indian War</a> became part of the <a href="/wiki/Seven_Years%27_War" title="Seven Years' War">Seven Years' War</a> (1756–1763). A militia from several British colonies, called the <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Regiment" title="Virginia Regiment">Virginia Regiment</a>, was led by then-Lieutenant Colonel <a href="/wiki/George_Washington" title="George Washington">George Washington</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAnderson200042.E2.80.9343_77-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAnderson200042.E2.80.9343-77">[77]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Statehood">Statehood</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Patrick_Henry_Rothermel.jpg"><img alt="Upper-class middle-aged man dressed in a bright red cloak speaks before an assembly of other angry men. The subject's right hand is raise high in gesture toward the balcony." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="750" data-file-width="580" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Patrick_Henry_Rothermel.jpg/170px-Patrick_Henry_Rothermel.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Patrick_Henry_Rothermel.jpg/255px-Patrick_Henry_Rothermel.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Patrick_Henry_Rothermel.jpg/340px-Patrick_Henry_Rothermel.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Patrick_Henry_Rothermel.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
1851 painting of <a href="/wiki/Patrick_Henry" title="Patrick Henry">Patrick Henry</a>'s speech before the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Burgesses" title="House of Burgesses">House of Burgesses</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Resolves" title="Virginia Resolves">Virginia Resolves</a> against the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stamp_Act_of_1765" title="Stamp Act of 1765">Stamp Act of 1765</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_Great_Britain" title="Parliament of Great Britain">British Parliament's</a> efforts to levy new taxes following the <a href="/wiki/French_and_Indian_War" title="French and Indian War">French and Indian War</a> were deeply unpopular in the colonies. In the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Burgesses" title="House of Burgesses">House of Burgesses</a>, opposition to <a href="/wiki/No_taxation_without_representation" title="No taxation without representation">taxation without representation</a> was led by <a href="/wiki/Patrick_Henry" title="Patrick Henry">Patrick Henry</a> and <a href="/wiki/Richard_Henry_Lee" title="Richard Henry Lee">Richard Henry Lee</a>, among others.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> Virginians began to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Committee_of_correspondence" title="Committee of correspondence">coordinate their actions</a> with other colonies in 1773, and sent delegates to the <a href="/wiki/Continental_Congress" title="Continental Congress">Continental Congress</a> the following year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGutzman200724.E2.80.9329_79-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGutzman200724.E2.80.9329-79">[79]</a></sup> After the House of Burgesses was dissolved by the royal governor in 1774, Virginia's revolutionary leaders continued to govern via the <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Conventions" title="Virginia Conventions">Virginia Conventions</a>. On May 15, 1776, the Convention declared Virginia's independence from the British Empire and adopted <a href="/wiki/George_Mason" title="George Mason">George Mason</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Declaration_of_Rights" title="Virginia Declaration of Rights">Virginia Declaration of Rights</a>, which was then included in a new constitution.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHeinemannKolpParent.2C_Jr.Shade2007125.E2.80.93133_80-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHeinemannKolpParent.2C_Jr.Shade2007125.E2.80.93133-80">[80]</a></sup> Another Virginian, <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Jefferson" title="Thomas Jefferson">Thomas Jefferson</a>, drew upon Mason's work in drafting the national <a href="/wiki/United_States_Declaration_of_Independence" title="United States Declaration of Independence">Declaration of Independence</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mason_81-0"><a href="#cite_note-mason-81">[81]</a></sup></p>
<p>When the <a href="/wiki/American_Revolutionary_War" title="American Revolutionary War">American Revolutionary War</a> began, <a href="/wiki/George_Washington" title="George Washington">George Washington</a> was selected to head the <a href="/wiki/Continental_Army" title="Continental Army">colonial army</a>. During the war, the capital was moved to <a href="/wiki/Richmond,_Virginia" title="Richmond, Virginia">Richmond</a> at the urging of Governor Thomas Jefferson, who feared that Williamsburg's coastal location would make it vulnerable to British attack.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECooper200758_82-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECooper200758-82">[82]</a></sup> In 1781, the combined action of <a href="/wiki/Continental_Army" title="Continental Army">Continental</a> and French land and naval forces trapped the British army on the <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Peninsula" title="Virginia Peninsula">Virginia Peninsula</a>, where troops under George Washington and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Comte_de_Rochambeau" title="Comte de Rochambeau">Comte de Rochambeau</a> defeated British <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/General_Cornwallis" title="General Cornwallis">General Cornwallis</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Yorktown" title="Siege of Yorktown">Siege of Yorktown</a>. His surrender on October 19, 1781 led to <a href="/wiki/Peace_of_Paris_(1783)" title="Peace of Paris (1783)">peace negotiations in Paris</a> and secured the independence of the colonies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHeinemannKolpParent.2C_Jr.Shade2007131.E2.80.93133_83-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHeinemannKolpParent.2C_Jr.Shade2007131.E2.80.93133-83">[83]</a></sup></p>
<p>Virginians were instrumental in writing the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Constitution" title="United States Constitution">United States Constitution</a>. <a href="/wiki/James_Madison" title="James Madison">James Madison</a> drafted the <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Plan" title="Virginia Plan">Virginia Plan</a> in 1787 and the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Bill_of_Rights" title="United States Bill of Rights">Bill of Rights</a> in 1789.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mason_81-1"><a href="#cite_note-mason-81">[81]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Ratifying_Convention" title="Virginia Ratifying Convention">Virginia ratified</a> the Constitution on June 25, 1788. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Three-fifths_compromise" title="Three-fifths compromise">three-fifths compromise</a> ensured that Virginia, with its large number of slaves, initially had the largest bloc in the <a href="/wiki/United_States_House_of_Representatives" title="United States House of Representatives">House of Representatives</a>. Together with the <a href="/wiki/Virginia_dynasty" title="Virginia dynasty">Virginia dynasty</a> of presidents, this gave the Commonwealth national importance. In 1790, both Virginia and Maryland ceded territory to form the new <a href="/wiki/Washington,_D.C." title="Washington, D.C.">District of Columbia</a>, though the Virginian area was <a href="/wiki/District_of_Columbia_retrocession" title="District of Columbia retrocession">retroceded</a> in 1846.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWallenstein2007104_84-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWallenstein2007104-84">[84]</a></sup> Virginia is called "Mother of States" because of its role in being carved into states like <a href="/wiki/Kentucky" title="Kentucky">Kentucky</a>, which became the 15th state in 1792, and for the numbers of <a href="/wiki/American_pioneer" title="American pioneer">American pioneers</a> born in Virginia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Robertson_85-0"><a href="#cite_note-Robertson-85">[85]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Civil_War_and_aftermath">Civil War and aftermath</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Virginia_in_the_American_Civil_War" title="Virginia in the American Civil War">Virginia in the American Civil War</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Union_soldiers_entrenched_along_the_west_bank_of_the_Rappahannock_River_at_Fredericksburg,_Virginia_(111-B-157).jpg"><img alt="Dozens of soldiers in coats and hats crowd a trench while two others stand tall to the right of the trench." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="935" data-file-width="1404" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Union_soldiers_entrenched_along_the_west_bank_of_the_Rappahannock_River_at_Fredericksburg%2C_Virginia_%28111-B-157%29.jpg/220px-Union_soldiers_entrenched_along_the_west_bank_of_the_Rappahannock_River_at_Fredericksburg%2C_Virginia_%28111-B-157%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Union_soldiers_entrenched_along_the_west_bank_of_the_Rappahannock_River_at_Fredericksburg%2C_Virginia_%28111-B-157%29.jpg/330px-Union_soldiers_entrenched_along_the_west_bank_of_the_Rappahannock_River_at_Fredericksburg%2C_Virginia_%28111-B-157%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Union_soldiers_entrenched_along_the_west_bank_of_the_Rappahannock_River_at_Fredericksburg%2C_Virginia_%28111-B-157%29.jpg/440px-Union_soldiers_entrenched_along_the_west_bank_of_the_Rappahannock_River_at_Fredericksburg%2C_Virginia_%28111-B-157%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Union_soldiers_entrenched_along_the_west_bank_of_the_Rappahannock_River_at_Fredericksburg,_Virginia_(111-B-157).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Union soldiers before Marye's Heights, <a href="/wiki/Second_Battle_of_Fredericksburg" title="Second Battle of Fredericksburg">Fredericksburg</a> in May 1863</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In addition to agriculture, slave labor was increasingly used in mining, shipbuilding and other industries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDavis2006125.2C_208.E2.80.93210_86-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDavis2006125.2C_208.E2.80.93210-86">[86]</a></sup> The execution of <a href="/wiki/Gabriel_Prosser" title="Gabriel Prosser">Gabriel Prosser</a> in 1800, <a href="/wiki/Nat_Turner%27s_slave_rebellion" title="Nat Turner's slave rebellion">Nat Turner's slave rebellion</a> in 1831 and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/John_Brown%27s_Raid_on_Harpers_Ferry" title="John Brown's Raid on Harpers Ferry">John Brown's Raid on Harpers Ferry</a> in 1859 marked the growing social discontent over slavery and its role in the <a href="/wiki/Plantation_economy" title="Plantation economy">plantation economy</a>. By 1860, almost half a million people, roughly 31% of the total population of Virginia, were enslaved.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hc_87-0"><a href="#cite_note-hc-87">[87]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMorgan1998490_88-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMorgan1998490-88">[88]</a></sup> This division contributed to the start of the <a href="/wiki/American_Civil_War" title="American Civil War">American Civil War</a>.</p>
<p>Virginia voted to secede from the United States on April 17, 1861, after the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Fort_Sumter" title="Battle of Fort Sumter">Battle of Fort Sumter</a> and <a href="/wiki/Abraham_Lincoln" title="Abraham Lincoln">Abraham Lincoln</a>'s call for volunteers. On April 24, Virginia joined the <a href="/wiki/Confederate_States_of_America" title="Confederate States of America">Confederate States of America</a>, which chose Richmond as its capital.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Robertson_85-1"><a href="#cite_note-Robertson-85">[85]</a></sup> After the 1861 <a href="/wiki/Wheeling_Convention" title="Wheeling Convention">Wheeling Convention</a>, 48 counties in the northwest separated to form a new state of <a href="/wiki/West_Virginia" title="West Virginia">West Virginia</a>, which chose to remain loyal to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Union_(Civil_War)" title="Union (Civil War)">Union</a>. Virginian general <a href="/wiki/Robert_E._Lee" title="Robert E. Lee">Robert E. Lee</a> took command of the <a href="/wiki/Army_of_Northern_Virginia" title="Army of Northern Virginia">Army of Northern Virginia</a> in 1862, and led invasions into Union territory, ultimately becoming commander of all Confederate forces. During the war, more battles were fought in Virginia than anywhere else, including <a href="/wiki/First_Battle_of_Bull_Run" title="First Battle of Bull Run">Bull Run</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Seven_Days_Battles" title="Seven Days Battles">Seven Days Battles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Chancellorsville" title="Battle of Chancellorsville">Chancellorsville</a>, and the concluding <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Appomattox_Court_House" title="Battle of Appomattox Court House">Battle of Appomattox Court House</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGoodwin20124_89-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGoodwin20124-89">[89]</a></sup> After the <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Petersburg" title="Siege of Petersburg">capture of Richmond</a> in April 1865, the state capital was briefly moved to <a href="/wiki/Lynchburg,_Virginia" title="Lynchburg, Virginia">Lynchburg</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> while the Confederate leadership fled to <a href="/wiki/Danville,_Virginia" title="Danville, Virginia">Danville</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobertson1993170_91-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobertson1993170-91">[91]</a></sup> Virginia was formally restored to the United States in 1870, due to the work of the <a href="/wiki/Committee_of_Nine" title="Committee of Nine">Committee of Nine</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHeinemannKolpParent.2C_Jr.Shade2007249.E2.80.93250_92-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHeinemannKolpParent.2C_Jr.Shade2007249.E2.80.93250-92">[92]</a></sup></p>
<p>During the post-war <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Reconstruction_era_of_the_United_States" title="Reconstruction era of the United States">Reconstruction era</a>, Virginia adopted a constitution which provided for free public schools, and guaranteed political, civil, and <a href="/wiki/Voting_rights_in_the_United_States" title="Voting rights in the United States">voting rights</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMorgan1992160.E2.80.93166_93-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMorgan1992160.E2.80.93166-93">[93]</a></sup> The populist <a href="/wiki/Readjuster_Party" title="Readjuster Party">Readjuster Party</a> ran an inclusive coalition until the conservative white <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_of_Virginia" title="Democratic Party of Virginia">Democratic Party</a> gained power after 1883.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDaileyGilmoreSimon200090.E2.80.9396_94-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDaileyGilmoreSimon200090.E2.80.9396-94">[94]</a></sup> It passed segregationist <a href="/wiki/Jim_Crow_laws" title="Jim Crow laws">Jim Crow laws</a> and in 1902 rewrote the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Virginia" title="Constitution of Virginia">Constitution of Virginia</a> to include a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Poll_tax_(United_States)" title="Poll tax (United States)">poll tax</a> and other voter registration measures that effectively <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Disfranchisement_after_the_Civil_War" title="Disfranchisement after the Civil War">disfranchised</a> most African Americans and many poor European Americans.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWallenstein2007253.E2.80.93254_95-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWallenstein2007253.E2.80.93254-95">[95]</a></sup> Though their schools and public services were segregated and underfunded due to a lack of political representation, African Americans were able to unite in communities and take a greater role in Virginia society.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDavis2006328.E2.80.93329_96-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDavis2006328.E2.80.93329-96">[96]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Post-Reconstruction">Post-Reconstruction</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:USS_Virginia_in_port.jpg"><img alt="A white battleship with three smokestacks and two tall masts sitting in port." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="5567" data-file-width="7804" height="157" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/USS_Virginia_in_port.jpg/220px-USS_Virginia_in_port.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/USS_Virginia_in_port.jpg/330px-USS_Virginia_in_port.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/USS_Virginia_in_port.jpg/440px-USS_Virginia_in_port.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:USS_Virginia_in_port.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Many <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pre-Dreadnought" title="Pre-Dreadnought">Pre-Dreadnought</a> and <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>-era warships were built in <a href="/wiki/Newport_News,_Virginia" title="Newport News, Virginia">Newport News</a>, including the <a href="/wiki/USS_Virginia_(BB-13)" title="USS Virginia (BB-13)">USS <i>Virginia</i></a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>New economic forces also changed the Commonwealth. Virginian <a href="/wiki/James_Albert_Bonsack" title="James Albert Bonsack">James Albert Bonsack</a> invented the tobacco cigarette rolling machine in 1880 leading to new industrial scale production centered on Richmond. In 1886, railroad magnate <a href="/wiki/Collis_Potter_Huntington" title="Collis Potter Huntington">Collis Potter Huntington</a> founded <a href="/wiki/Newport_News_Shipbuilding" title="Newport News Shipbuilding">Newport News Shipbuilding</a>, which was responsible for building six major <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>-era battleships for the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Navy" title="U.S. Navy">U.S. Navy</a> from 1907 to 1923.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> During the war, <a href="/wiki/German_Empire" title="German Empire">German</a> submarines like <a href="/wiki/SM_U-151" title="SM U-151">U-151</a> attacked ships outside the port.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFeuer199950.E2.80.9352_98-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFeuer199950.E2.80.9352-98">[98]</a></sup> In 1926, Dr. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/W.A.R._Goodwin" title="W.A.R. Goodwin">W.A.R. Goodwin</a>, rector of Williamsburg's <a href="/wiki/Bruton_Parish_Church" title="Bruton Parish Church">Bruton Parish Church</a>, began restoration of colonial-era buildings in the historic district with financial backing of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/John_D._Rockefeller,_Jr." title="John D. Rockefeller, Jr.">John D. Rockefeller, Jr.</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGoodwin2012238_99-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGoodwin2012238-99">[99]</a></sup> Though their project, like others in the state, had to contend with the <a href="/wiki/Great_Depression" title="Great Depression">Great Depression</a> and <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, work continued as <a href="/wiki/Colonial_Williamsburg" title="Colonial Williamsburg">Colonial Williamsburg</a> became a major tourist attraction.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGreenspan200937.E2.80.9343_100-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGreenspan200937.E2.80.9343-100">[100]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Virginia_Civil_Rights_Memorial_wide.jpg"><img alt="Bronze sculptures of seven figures marching stand around a large rectangular block of white engraved granite." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="273" data-file-width="365" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/48/Virginia_Civil_Rights_Memorial_wide.jpg/220px-Virginia_Civil_Rights_Memorial_wide.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/48/Virginia_Civil_Rights_Memorial_wide.jpg/330px-Virginia_Civil_Rights_Memorial_wide.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/4/48/Virginia_Civil_Rights_Memorial_wide.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Virginia_Civil_Rights_Memorial_wide.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Civil_Rights_Memorial" title="Virginia Civil Rights Memorial">Virginia Civil Rights Memorial</a> was erected in 2008 to commemorate the protests which led to school desegregation.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Protests started by <a href="/wiki/Barbara_Rose_Johns" title="Barbara Rose Johns">Barbara Rose Johns</a> in 1951 in <a href="/wiki/Farmville,_Virginia" title="Farmville, Virginia">Farmville</a> against segregated schools led to the lawsuit <i><a href="/wiki/Davis_v._County_School_Board_of_Prince_Edward_County" title="Davis v. County School Board of Prince Edward County">Davis v. County School Board of Prince Edward County</a></i>. This case, filed by Richmond natives <a href="/wiki/Spottswood_William_Robinson_III" title="Spottswood William Robinson III">Spottswood Robinson</a> and <a href="/wiki/Oliver_Hill" title="Oliver Hill">Oliver Hill</a>, was decided in 1954 with <i><a href="/wiki/Brown_v._Board_of_Education" title="Brown v. Board of Education">Brown v. Board of Education</a></i>, which rejected the segregationist doctrine of "<a href="/wiki/Separate_but_equal" title="Separate but equal">separate but equal</a>". But, in 1958, under the policy of "<a href="/wiki/Massive_resistance" title="Massive resistance">massive resistance</a>" led by the influential segregationist Senator <a href="/wiki/Harry_F._Byrd" title="Harry F. Byrd">Harry F. Byrd</a> and his <a href="/wiki/Byrd_Organization" title="Byrd Organization">Byrd Organization</a>, the Commonwealth prohibited <a href="/wiki/Desegregation" title="Desegregation">desegregated</a> local schools from receiving state funding.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWallenstein2007340.E2.80.93341_101-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWallenstein2007340.E2.80.93341-101">[101]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Civil_Rights_Movement" title="Civil Rights Movement">Civil Rights Movement</a> gained many participants in the 1960s. It achieved the moral force and support to gain passage of national legislation with the <a href="/wiki/Civil_Rights_Act_of_1964" title="Civil Rights Act of 1964">Civil Rights Act of 1964</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Voting_Rights_Act_of_1965" title="Voting Rights Act of 1965">Voting Rights Act of 1965</a>. In 1964 the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_Supreme_Court" title="United States Supreme Court">United States Supreme Court</a> ordered <a href="/wiki/Prince_Edward_County,_Virginia" title="Prince Edward County, Virginia">Prince Edward County</a> and others to <a href="/wiki/Racial_integration" title="Racial integration">integrate</a> schools.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWallenstein2007357_102-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWallenstein2007357-102">[102]</a></sup> In 1967, the Court also struck down the state's ban on <a href="/wiki/Interracial_marriage_in_the_United_States" title="Interracial marriage in the United States">interracial marriage</a> with <i><a href="/wiki/Loving_v._Virginia" title="Loving v. Virginia">Loving v. Virginia</a></i>. From 1969 to 1971, state legislators under Governor <a href="/wiki/Mills_Godwin" title="Mills Godwin">Mills Godwin</a> rewrote the constitution, after goals such as the repeal of <a href="/wiki/Jim_Crow_laws" title="Jim Crow laws">Jim Crow laws</a> had been achieved. In 1989, <a href="/wiki/Douglas_Wilder" title="Douglas Wilder">Douglas Wilder</a> became the first African American elected as governor in the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHeinemannKolpParent.2C_Jr.Shade2007359.E2.80.93366_103-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHeinemannKolpParent.2C_Jr.Shade2007359.E2.80.93366-103">[103]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a> led to the expansion of national defense government programs housed in offices in Northern Virginia near Washington, D.C., and correlative population growth.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAccordino200076.E2.80.9378_104-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAccordino200076.E2.80.9378-104">[104]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Central_Intelligence_Agency" title="Central Intelligence Agency">Central Intelligence Agency</a> in <a href="/wiki/Langley,_Virginia" title="Langley, Virginia">Langley</a> was involved in various <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_events_in_the_Cold_War" title="Timeline of events in the Cold War">Cold War events</a>, including as the target of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/History_of_Soviet_and_Russian_espionage_in_the_United_States" title="History of Soviet and Russian espionage in the United States">Soviet espionage activities</a>. Also among the federal developments was <a href="/wiki/The_Pentagon" title="The Pentagon">the Pentagon</a>, built during World War II as the headquarters for the Department of Defense. It was one of the targets of the <a href="/wiki/September_11_attacks" title="September 11 attacks">September 11 attacks</a>; 189 people died at the site when a jet passenger plane was crashed into the building.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup></p>

<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Virginia-Population.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="344" data-file-width="792" height="130" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Virginia-Population.svg/300px-Virginia-Population.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Virginia-Population.svg/450px-Virginia-Population.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Virginia-Population.svg/600px-Virginia-Population.svg.png 2x" width="300"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Virginia-Population.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Virginia counties and cities by population in 2010</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Virginia is divided into 95 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_counties_in_Virginia" title="List of counties in Virginia">counties</a> and 38 <a href="/wiki/Independent_city_(United_States)" title="Independent city (United States)">independent cities</a>, the latter acting in many ways as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/County-equivalent" title="County-equivalent">county-equivalents</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup> This general method of treating cities and counties on par with each other is unique to Virginia; only three other <a href="/wiki/Independent_city_(United_States)#Other_states" title="Independent city (United States)">independent cities</a> exist elsewhere in the United States, each in a different state.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> Virginia limits the authority of cities and counties to countermand laws expressly allowed by the <a href="/wiki/Virginia_General_Assembly" title="Virginia General Assembly">Virginia General Assembly</a> under what is known as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dillon%27s_Rule" title="Dillon's Rule">Dillon's Rule</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> In addition to independent cities, there are also <a href="/wiki/List_of_towns_in_Virginia" title="List of towns in Virginia">incorporated <i>towns</i></a> which operate under their own governments, but are part of a county. Finally there are hundreds of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_unincorporated_towns_in_Virginia" title="List of unincorporated towns in Virginia">unincorporated communities</a> within the counties. Virginia does not have any further political subdivisions, such as villages or townships.</p>
<p>Virginia has 11 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Virginia_census_statistical_areas" title="Virginia census statistical areas">Metropolitan Statistical Areas</a>; <a href="/wiki/Northern_Virginia" title="Northern Virginia">Northern Virginia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hampton_Roads" title="Hampton Roads">Hampton Roads</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Richmond-Petersburg" title="Richmond-Petersburg">Richmond-Petersburg</a> are the three most populous. Richmond is the capital of Virginia, and its metropolitan area has a population of over 1.2 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-popnews_110-0"><a href="#cite_note-popnews-110">[110]</a></sup> As of 2010<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Virginia&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Beach,_Virginia" title="Virginia Beach, Virginia">Virginia Beach</a> is the most populous city in the Commonwealth, with <a href="/wiki/Norfolk,_Virginia" title="Norfolk, Virginia">Norfolk</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chesapeake,_Virginia" title="Chesapeake, Virginia">Chesapeake</a> second and third, respectively.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-c2009_111-0"><a href="#cite_note-c2009-111">[111]</a></sup> Norfolk forms the urban core of the Hampton Roads metropolitan area, which has a population over 1.6 million people and is the site of the world's largest naval base, <a href="/wiki/Naval_Station_Norfolk" title="Naval Station Norfolk">Naval Station Norfolk</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-popnews_110-1"><a href="#cite_note-popnews-110">[110]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hr_112-0"><a href="#cite_note-hr-112">[112]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Suffolk,_Virginia" title="Suffolk, Virginia">Suffolk</a>, which includes a portion of the <a href="/wiki/Great_Dismal_Swamp" title="Great Dismal Swamp">Great Dismal Swamp</a>, is the largest city by area at 429.1 square miles (1,111 km<sup>2</sup>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Fairfax_County,_Virginia" title="Fairfax County, Virginia">Fairfax County</a> is the most populous locality in Virginia, with over one million residents, although that does not include its <a href="/wiki/County_seat" title="County seat">county seat</a> Fairfax, which is one of the independent cities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup> Fairfax County has a major urban business and shopping center in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tysons_Corner" title="Tysons Corner">Tysons Corner</a>, Virginia's largest office market.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup> Neighboring <a href="/wiki/Prince_William_County,_Virginia" title="Prince William County, Virginia">Prince William County</a> is Virginia's second most populous county, with a population exceeding 450,000, and is home to <a href="/wiki/Marine_Corps_Base_Quantico" title="Marine Corps Base Quantico">Marine Corps Base Quantico</a>, the <a href="/wiki/FBI_Academy" title="FBI Academy">FBI Academy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Manassas_National_Battlefield_Park" title="Manassas National Battlefield Park">Manassas National Battlefield Park</a>. <a href="/wiki/Loudoun_County,_Virginia" title="Loudoun County, Virginia">Loudoun County</a>, with the county seat at <a href="/wiki/Leesburg,_Virginia" title="Leesburg, Virginia">Leesburg</a>, is both the fastest-growing county in Virginia and has the highest median household income ($114,204) in the country as of 2010<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Virginia&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ltm_116-0"><a href="#cite_note-ltm-116">[116]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Arlington_County,_Virginia" title="Arlington County, Virginia">Arlington County</a>, the smallest self-governing county in the United States by land area, is an urban community organized as a county.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Roanoke,_Virginia" title="Roanoke, Virginia">Roanoke</a> area, with an estimated population of 300,399, is the largest Metropolitan Statistical Area in western Virginia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup></p>
