<div class="mw-stack mobile-float-reset" style="box-sizing: border-box; float:right;">
<div style="overflow: hidden; margin: 1px;">
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Elizabeth_River_at_NNSY.jpg"><img alt="The nuclear-powered aircraft carrier USS Harry S. Truman (CVN-75) transits the Elizabeth River at Norfolk Naval Shipyard." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2100" data-file-width="1500" height="238" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Elizabeth_River_at_NNSY.jpg/170px-Elizabeth_River_at_NNSY.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Elizabeth_River_at_NNSY.jpg/255px-Elizabeth_River_at_NNSY.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Elizabeth_River_at_NNSY.jpg/340px-Elizabeth_River_at_NNSY.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Elizabeth_River_at_NNSY.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Hampton_Roads" title="Hampton Roads">Hampton Roads</a> metropolitan area is home to the first <a href="/wiki/British_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="British colonization of the Americas">British colony in the Americas</a>, and currently has a population exceeding 1.7 million.</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/United_States_Census_Bureau" title="United States Census Bureau">United States Census Bureau</a> estimates that the state population was 8,411,808 on July 1, 2016, a 5.1% increase since the <a href="/wiki/2010_United_States_Census" title="2010 United States Census">2010 United States Census</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PopEstUS_121-1"><a href="#cite_note-PopEstUS-121">[121]</a></sup> This includes an increase from net migration of 381,969 people into the Commonwealth since the <a href="/wiki/2010_United_States_Census" title="2010 United States Census">2010 census</a>. <a href="/wiki/Immigration_to_the_United_States" title="Immigration to the United States">Immigration</a> from outside the United States resulted in a net increase of 159,627 people, and migration within the country produced a net increase of 155,205 people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup> As of 2000, the <a href="/wiki/Center_of_population" title="Center of population">center of population</a> is located in <a href="/wiki/Goochland_County,_Virginia" title="Goochland County, Virginia">Goochland County</a>, near <a href="/wiki/Richmond,_Virginia" title="Richmond, Virginia">Richmond</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-census_123-0"><a href="#cite_note-census-123">[123]</a></sup></p>
<p>Aside from Virginia, the top birth state for Virginians is <a href="/wiki/New_York_(state)" title="New York (state)">New York</a>, having overtaken <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina" title="North Carolina">North Carolina</a> in the 1990s, with the <a href="/wiki/Northeastern_United_States" title="Northeastern United States">Northeast</a> accounting for the largest number of migrants into the state by region.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nytmigrationanddiaspora_124-0"><a href="#cite_note-nytmigrationanddiaspora-124">[124]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnicity">Ethnicity</span></h3>
<p>The state's most populous ethnic group, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Non-Hispanic_White" title="Non-Hispanic White">Non-Hispanic White</a>, has declined from 76% in 1990 to 62.7% in 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2015CensusQuickFacts_126-0"><a href="#cite_note-2015CensusQuickFacts-126">[126]</a></sup> In 2011, non-Hispanic Whites were involved in 50.9% of all the births.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup> People of <a href="/wiki/English_Americans" title="English Americans">English heritage</a> settled throughout the Commonwealth during the colonial period, and others of British and Irish heritage have since immigrated.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMillerSchrierBolingDoyle20036.2C_147_128-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMillerSchrierBolingDoyle20036.2C_147-128">[128]</a></sup> Those who self-identify as having "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/American_ethnicity" title="American ethnicity">American ethnicity</a>" are predominantly of English descent, but have ancestry that has been in North America for so long that they choose to identify simply as American.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup> Of the English immigrants to Virginia in the 17th century, 75% came as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indentured_servant" title="Indentured servant">indentured servants</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup> The western mountains have many settlements that were founded by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Scots-Irish_American" title="Scots-Irish American">Scots-Irish immigrants</a> before the <a href="/wiki/American_Revolution" title="American Revolution">American Revolution</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup> There are also sizable numbers of people of German descent in the northwestern mountains and <a href="/wiki/Shenandoah_Valley" title="Shenandoah Valley">Shenandoah Valley</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dutch_134-0"><a href="#cite_note-dutch-134">[134]</a></sup> and German ancestry was the most popular response on the 2010 <a href="/wiki/American_Community_Survey" title="American Community Survey">American Community Survey</a>, with 11.7%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ancestry_135-0"><a href="#cite_note-ancestry-135">[135]</a></sup> 2.9% of Virginians also describe themselves as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Biracial" title="Biracial">biracial</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-demographics_136-0"><a href="#cite_note-demographics-136">[136]</a></sup></p>
<p>The largest minority group in Virginia is African American, at 19.7% as of 2015<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Virginia&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2015CensusQuickFacts_126-1"><a href="#cite_note-2015CensusQuickFacts-126">[126]</a></sup> Most African American Virginians have been descendants of enslaved Africans who worked on tobacco, cotton, and <a href="/wiki/Hemp" title="Hemp">hemp</a> plantations. These men, women and children were brought from West and West-Central Africa, primarily from <a href="/wiki/Angola" title="Angola">Angola</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bight_of_Bonny" title="Bight of Bonny">Bight of Biafra</a>. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Igbo_American" title="Igbo American">Igbo</a> ethnic group of what is now southern <a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">Nigeria</a> were the single largest African group among slaves in Virginia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup> Though the black population was reduced by the <a href="/wiki/Great_Migration_(African_American)" title="Great Migration (African American)">Great Migration</a>, since 1965 there has been a reverse migration of blacks <a href="/wiki/New_Great_Migration" title="New Great Migration">returning south</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup> According to the <a href="/wiki/Pew_Research_Center" title="Pew Research Center">Pew Research Center</a>, the state has the highest concentration of black and white interracial marriages.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-blackwhite_139-0"><a href="#cite_note-blackwhite-139">[139]</a></sup></p>
<p>More recent immigration in the late 20th century and early 21st century has fueled new communities of Hispanics and Asians. As of 2015<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Virginia&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, 9.0% of Virginians are <a href="/wiki/Hispanic_and_Latino_Americans" title="Hispanic and Latino Americans">Hispanic</a> or Latino (of any race), and 6.5% are <a href="/wiki/Asian_people" title="Asian people">Asian</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2015CensusQuickFacts_126-2"><a href="#cite_note-2015CensusQuickFacts-126">[126]</a></sup> The state's Hispanic population rose by 92% from 2000 to 2010, with two-thirds of Hispanics living in <a href="/wiki/Northern_Virginia" title="Northern Virginia">Northern Virginia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-demographics_136-1"><a href="#cite_note-demographics-136">[136]</a></sup> Hispanic citizens in Virginia have higher median household incomes and educational attainment than the general Virginia population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hispanics_140-0"><a href="#cite_note-hispanics-140">[140]</a></sup> As far as Hispanic groups, there is a large <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Salvadoran_American" title="Salvadoran American">Salvadoran</a> population in the DC suburbs of Northern Virginia,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup> and a large <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Puerto_Rican_American" title="Puerto Rican American">Puerto Rican</a> population in the <a href="/wiki/Hampton_Roads" title="Hampton Roads">Hampton Roads</a> region of Southeast Virginia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup> Northern Virginia also has a significant population of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vietnamese_American" title="Vietnamese American">Vietnamese Americans</a>, whose major wave of immigration followed the <a href="/wiki/Vietnam_War" title="Vietnam War">Vietnam War</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Korean_American" title="Korean American">Korean Americans</a>, whose migration has been more recent and was induced in part by the quality school system.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Filipino_American" title="Filipino American">Filipino American</a> community has about 45,000 in the Hampton Roads area, many of whom have ties to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Navy" title="U.S. Navy">U.S. Navy</a> and armed forces.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup></p>
<p>Additionally, 0.5% of Virginians are <a href="/wiki/Native_Americans_in_the_United_States" title="Native Americans in the United States">American Indian</a> or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alaska_Native" title="Alaska Native">Alaska Native</a>, and 0.1% are <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Native_Hawaiian" title="Native Hawaiian">Native Hawaiian</a> or other <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Islander" title="Pacific Islander">Pacific Islander</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2015CensusQuickFacts_126-3"><a href="#cite_note-2015CensusQuickFacts-126">[126]</a></sup> Virginia has extended state recognition to eight <a href="/wiki/Native_American_tribes_in_Virginia" title="Native American tribes in Virginia">Native American tribes</a> resident in the state, though some lack federal recognition status. Most Native American groups are located in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tidewater_region_of_Virginia" title="Tidewater region of Virginia">Tidewater region</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup></p>

<p>As of 2011, 49.1% of Virginia's population younger than age 1 were minorities (meaning that they had at least one parent who was not non-Hispanic white).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Piedmont_region_of_Virginia" title="Piedmont region of Virginia">Piedmont</a> region is known for its dialect's strong influence on <a href="/wiki/Southern_American_English" title="Southern American English">Southern American English</a>. While a more homogenized <a href="/wiki/American_English" title="American English">American English</a> is found in urban areas, various accents are also used, including the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tidewater_accent" title="Tidewater accent">Tidewater accent</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Old_Virginia_accent" title="Old Virginia accent">Old Virginia accent</a>, and the anachronistic <a href="/wiki/Early_Modern_English" title="Early Modern English">Elizabethan</a> of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tangier_Island" title="Tangier Island">Tangier Island</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Miller_149-0"><a href="#cite_note-Miller-149">[149]</a></sup></p>
<p>As of 2010<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Virginia&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, 85.87% (6,299,127) of Virginia residents age 5 and older spoke <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a> at home as a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Primary_language" title="Primary language">primary language</a>, while 6.41% (470,058) spoke <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a>, 0.77% (56,518) <a href="/wiki/Korean_language" title="Korean language">Korean</a>, 0.63% (45,881) <a href="/wiki/Vietnamese_language" title="Vietnamese language">Vietnamese</a>, 0.57% (42,418) <a href="/wiki/Chinese_language" title="Chinese language">Chinese</a> (which includes <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Standard_Mandarin" title="Standard Mandarin">Mandarin</a>), and <a href="/wiki/Tagalog_language" title="Tagalog language">Tagalog</a> was spoken as a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Main_language" title="Main language">main language</a> by 0.56% (40,724) of the population over the age of five. In total, 14.13% (1,036,442) of Virginia's population age 5 and older spoke a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mother_language" title="Mother language">mother language</a> other than English.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MLA_Data_150-0"><a href="#cite_note-MLA_Data-150">[150]</a></sup> English was passed as the Commonwealth's official language by statutes in 1981 and again in 1996, though the status is not mandated by the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Virginia" title="Constitution of Virginia">Constitution of Virginia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJoseph200663_151-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJoseph200663-151">[151]</a></sup></p>

<td align="right">0.5%</td>

<td colspan="2"><a href="/wiki/Irreligion" title="Irreligion">Unaffiliated</a></td>
<td align="right">18%</td>

<p>Virginia is predominantly Christian and <a href="/wiki/Protestantism" title="Protestantism">Protestant</a>; <a href="/wiki/Baptists" title="Baptists">Baptists</a> are the largest single group with 27% of the population as of 2008<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Virginia&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aris_152-1"><a href="#cite_note-aris-152">[152]</a></sup> Baptist congregations in Virginia have 763,655 members.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-www.thearda.com_153-0"><a href="#cite_note-www.thearda.com-153">[153]</a></sup> Baptist denominational groups in Virginia include the <a href="/wiki/Baptist_General_Association_of_Virginia" title="Baptist General Association of Virginia">Baptist General Association of Virginia</a>, with about 1,400 member churches, which supports both the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Baptist_Convention" title="Southern Baptist Convention">Southern Baptist Convention</a> and the moderate <a href="/wiki/Cooperative_Baptist_Fellowship" title="Cooperative Baptist Fellowship">Cooperative Baptist Fellowship</a>; and the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Baptist_Conservatives_of_Virginia" title="Southern Baptist Conservatives of Virginia">Southern Baptist Conservatives of Virginia</a> with more than 500 affiliated churches, which supports the Southern Baptist Convention.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154"><a href="#cite_note-154">[154]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155"><a href="#cite_note-155">[155]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism_in_the_United_States" title="Roman Catholicism in the United States">Roman Catholics</a> are the second-largest religious group with 673,853 members.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-www.thearda.com_153-1"><a href="#cite_note-www.thearda.com-153">[153]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Diocese_of_Arlington" title="Roman Catholic Diocese of Arlington">Roman Catholic Diocese of Arlington</a> includes most of Northern Virginia's Catholic churches, while the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Diocese_of_Richmond" title="Roman Catholic Diocese of Richmond">Diocese of Richmond</a> covers the rest.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Christchurchalexandria.jpg"><img alt="An 18th-century red brick church with white steeple behind a modern road in autumn." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1478" data-file-width="1971" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Christchurchalexandria.jpg/220px-Christchurchalexandria.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Christchurchalexandria.jpg/330px-Christchurchalexandria.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Christchurchalexandria.jpg/440px-Christchurchalexandria.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Christchurchalexandria.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Christ_Church_(Alexandria,_Virginia)" title="Christ Church (Alexandria, Virginia)">Christ Church in Alexandria</a> was frequented by <a href="/wiki/George_Washington" title="George Washington">George Washington</a> and <a href="/wiki/Robert_E._Lee" title="Robert E. Lee">Robert E. Lee</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Virginia Conference is the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Annual_Conference" title="Annual Conference">regional body</a> of the <a href="/wiki/United_Methodist_Church" title="United Methodist Church">United Methodist Church</a> in most of the Commonwealth, while the Holston Conference represents much of extreme Southwest Virginia. The <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Synod" title="Virginia Synod">Virginia Synod</a> is responsible for the congregations of the <a href="/wiki/Evangelical_Lutheran_Church_in_America" title="Evangelical Lutheran Church in America">Lutheran Church</a>. <a href="/wiki/Presbyterianism" title="Presbyterianism">Presbyterian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pentecostalism" title="Pentecostalism">Pentecostal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Congregational_church" title="Congregational church">Congregationalist</a>, and Episcopalian adherents each composed less than 2% of the population as of 2010<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Virginia&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-www.thearda.com_153-2"><a href="#cite_note-www.thearda.com-153">[153]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Episcopal_Diocese_of_Virginia" title="Episcopal Diocese of Virginia">Episcopal Diocese of Virginia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Episcopal_Diocese_of_Southern_Virginia" title="Episcopal Diocese of Southern Virginia">Southern Virginia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Episcopal_Diocese_of_Southwestern_Virginia" title="Episcopal Diocese of Southwestern Virginia">Southwestern Virginia</a> support the various <a href="/wiki/Episcopal_Church_(United_States)" title="Episcopal Church (United States)">Episcopal churches</a>.</p>
<p>In November 2006, 15 conservative Episcopal churches voted to split from the Diocese of Virginia over the ordination of openly <a href="/wiki/Gay_bishops" title="Gay bishops">gay bishops</a> and clergy in other dioceses of the Episcopal Church; these churches continue to claim affiliation with the larger <a href="/wiki/Anglican_Communion" title="Anglican Communion">Anglican Communion</a> through <a href="/wiki/Anglican_realignment" title="Anglican realignment">other bodies outside the United States</a>. Though Virginia law allows parishioners to determine their church's affiliation, the diocese claimed the secessionist churches' buildings and properties. The resulting property law case, ultimately decided in favor of the mainline diocese, was a test for Episcopal churches nationwide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156"><a href="#cite_note-156">[156]</a></sup></p>
<p>Among other religions, adherents of <a href="/wiki/The_Church_of_Jesus_Christ_of_Latter-day_Saints" title="The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints">The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints</a> constitute 1% of the population, with 200 <a href="/wiki/The_Church_of_Jesus_Christ_of_Latter-day_Saints_in_Virginia" title="The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints in Virginia">congregations in Virginia</a> as of 2017<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Virginia&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157"><a href="#cite_note-157">[157]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Fairfax_Station,_Virginia" title="Fairfax Station, Virginia">Fairfax Station</a> is the site of the <a href="/wiki/Ekoji_Buddhist_Temple" title="Ekoji Buddhist Temple">Ekoji Buddhist Temple</a>, of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jodo_Shinshu" title="Jodo Shinshu">Jodo Shinshu</a> school, and the Hindu <a href="/wiki/Durga" title="Durga">Durga</a> Temple. While the state's Jewish population is small, organized Jewish sites date to 1789 with <a href="/wiki/Congregation_Beth_Ahabah" title="Congregation Beth Ahabah">Congregation Beth Ahabah</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEOlitzky1996359_158-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEOlitzky1996359-158">[158]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Muslims" title="Muslims">Muslims</a> are a growing religious group throughout the Commonwealth through immigration.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159"><a href="#cite_note-159">[159]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Megachurch" title="Megachurch">Megachurches</a> in the Commonwealth include <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Road_Baptist_Church" title="Thomas Road Baptist Church">Thomas Road Baptist Church</a>, <a href="/wiki/Immanuel_Bible_Church" title="Immanuel Bible Church">Immanuel Bible Church</a>, and <a href="/wiki/McLean_Bible_Church" title="McLean Bible Church">McLean Bible Church</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160"><a href="#cite_note-160">[160]</a></sup> Several Christian universities are also based in the state, including <a href="/wiki/Regent_University" title="Regent University">Regent University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Liberty_University" title="Liberty University">Liberty University</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Lynchburg_College" title="Lynchburg College">Lynchburg College</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Virginia" title="Economy of Virginia">Economy of Virginia</a></div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Virginia_locations_by_per_capita_income" title="Virginia locations by per capita income">Virginia locations by per capita income</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Virginia-Median_household_income.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="344" data-file-width="792" height="130" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Virginia-Median_household_income.svg/300px-Virginia-Median_household_income.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Virginia-Median_household_income.svg/450px-Virginia-Median_household_income.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Virginia-Median_household_income.svg/600px-Virginia-Median_household_income.svg.png 2x" width="300"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Virginia-Median_household_income.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Virginia counties and cities by median household income (2010).</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Virginia is an <a href="/wiki/At-will_employment" title="At-will employment">employment-at-will</a> state;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161"><a href="#cite_note-161">[161]</a></sup> its economy has diverse sources of income, including local and federal government, military, farming and business. Virginia has 4.1 million civilian workers, and one-third of the jobs are in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Service_sector" title="Service sector">service sector</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-energy_162-0"><a href="#cite_note-energy-162">[162]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ng_163-0"><a href="#cite_note-ng-163">[163]</a></sup> The unemployment rate in Virginia as of 2017<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Virginia&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> is 3.8%, which is below the national average.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164"><a href="#cite_note-164">[164]</a></sup> The second fastest job growth town in the nation is <a href="/wiki/Leesburg,_Virginia" title="Leesburg, Virginia">Leesburg</a>, as of 2011<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Virginia&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165"><a href="#cite_note-165">[165]</a></sup> The Gross Domestic Product of Virginia was $452 billion in 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166"><a href="#cite_note-166">[166]</a></sup> According to the <a href="/wiki/Bureau_of_Economic_Analysis" title="Bureau of Economic Analysis">Bureau of Economic Analysis</a>, Virginia had the most counties in the top 100 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Highest-income_counties_in_the_United_States" title="Highest-income counties in the United States">wealthiest in the United States</a> at sixteen counties based upon median income in 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-167"><a href="#cite_note-167">[167]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Northern_Virginia" title="Northern Virginia">Northern Virginia</a> is the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Highest-income_counties_in_the_United_States" title="Highest-income counties in the United States">highest-income region</a> in Virginia, having six of the twenty <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Highest-income_counties_in_the_United_States" title="Highest-income counties in the United States">highest-income counties in the United States</a>, including the two highest as of 2008<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Virginia&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-168"><a href="#cite_note-168">[168]</a></sup> According to CNN Money Magazine the highest-income town in the nation is <a href="/wiki/Great_Falls,_Virginia" title="Great Falls, Virginia">Great Falls</a>, as of 2011<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Virginia&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-169"><a href="#cite_note-169">[169]</a></sup> According to a 2013 study by Phoenix Marketing International, Virginia had the seventh-largest number of millionaires per capita in the United States, with a ratio of 6.64%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-170"><a href="#cite_note-170">[170]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Government">Government</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_Pentagon_January_2008.jpg"><img alt="Aerial view of the huge five-sided building and its multiple rings. Parking lots and highways stretch away from it." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1482" data-file-width="2592" height="126" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/The_Pentagon_January_2008.jpg/220px-The_Pentagon_January_2008.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/The_Pentagon_January_2008.jpg/330px-The_Pentagon_January_2008.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/The_Pentagon_January_2008.jpg/440px-The_Pentagon_January_2008.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:The_Pentagon_January_2008.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Defense" title="United States Department of Defense">Department of Defense</a> is headquartered in <a href="/wiki/Arlington_County,_Virginia" title="Arlington County, Virginia">Arlington</a> at <a href="/wiki/The_Pentagon" title="The Pentagon">The Pentagon</a>, the world's largest office building.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-171"><a href="#cite_note-171">[171]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Virginia has the highest defense spending of any state per capita, providing the Commonwealth with around 900,000 jobs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lovehate_172-0"><a href="#cite_note-lovehate-172">[172]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fedspend_173-0"><a href="#cite_note-fedspend-173">[173]</a></sup> Approximately 12% of all <a href="/wiki/Government_procurement_in_the_United_States" title="Government procurement in the United States">U.S. federal procurement</a> money is spent in Virginia, the second-highest amount after California.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fedspend_173-1"><a href="#cite_note-fedspend-173">[173]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-weighdefense_174-0"><a href="#cite_note-weighdefense-174">[174]</a></sup> Many Virginians work for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_United_States_federal_agencies" title="List of United States federal agencies">federal agencies</a> in <a href="/wiki/Northern_Virginia" title="Northern Virginia">Northern Virginia</a>, which include the <a href="/wiki/Central_Intelligence_Agency" title="Central Intelligence Agency">Central Intelligence Agency</a> and the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Defense" title="United States Department of Defense">Department of Defense</a>, as well as the <a href="/wiki/National_Science_Foundation" title="National Science Foundation">National Science Foundation</a>, the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Geological_Survey" title="United States Geological Survey">United States Geological Survey</a> and the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Patent_and_Trademark_Office" title="United States Patent and Trademark Office">United States Patent and Trademark Office</a>. Many others work for <a href="/wiki/Government_contractor" title="Government contractor">government contractors</a>, including defense and security firms, which hold more than 15,000 federal contracts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fedjobs_175-0"><a href="#cite_note-fedjobs-175">[175]</a></sup></p>
<p>Virginia has one of the highest concentrations of veterans of any state,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-176"><a href="#cite_note-176">[176]</a></sup> and is second to <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">California</a> in total Department of Defense employees.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-weighdefense_174-1"><a href="#cite_note-weighdefense-174">[174]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-177"><a href="#cite_note-177">[177]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Hampton_Roads" title="Hampton Roads">Hampton Roads</a> area has the largest concentration of military personnel and assets of any metropolitan area in the world,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-178"><a href="#cite_note-178">[178]</a></sup> including the largest naval base in the world, <a href="/wiki/Naval_Station_Norfolk" title="Naval Station Norfolk">Naval Station Norfolk</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hr_112-1"><a href="#cite_note-hr-112">[112]</a></sup> In its state government, Virginia employs 106,143 public employees, who combined have a median income of $44,656 as of 2013<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Virginia&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-179"><a href="#cite_note-179">[179]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Business">Business</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Virginia_Beach_waterfront.jpg"><img alt="High-rise hotels line the ocean front covered with colorful beach-goers." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="3008" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Virginia_Beach_waterfront.jpg/220px-Virginia_Beach_waterfront.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Virginia_Beach_waterfront.jpg/330px-Virginia_Beach_waterfront.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Virginia_Beach_waterfront.jpg/440px-Virginia_Beach_waterfront.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Virginia_Beach_waterfront.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Ocean tourism is an important sector of <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Beach,_Virginia" title="Virginia Beach, Virginia">Virginia Beach's</a> economy.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Virginia has the highest concentration of technology workers of any state,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-180"><a href="#cite_note-180">[180]</a></sup> and the fourth-highest number of technology workers after <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">California</a>, <a href="/wiki/Texas" title="Texas">Texas</a>, and <a href="/wiki/New_York_(state)" title="New York (state)">New York</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-181"><a href="#cite_note-181">[181]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Integrated_circuit" title="Integrated circuit">Computer chips</a> became the state's highest-grossing export in 2006, surpassing its traditional top exports of coal and tobacco combined,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-chips_182-0"><a href="#cite_note-chips-182">[182]</a></sup> reaching a total export value of $717 million in 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-chips_census_183-0"><a href="#cite_note-chips_census-183">[183]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Northern_Virginia" title="Northern Virginia">Northern Virginia</a>, once considered the state's dairy capital, now hosts software, communication technology, defense contracting companies, particularly in the <a href="/wiki/Dulles_Technology_Corridor" title="Dulles Technology Corridor">Dulles Technology Corridor</a>.</p>
<p>The state has the highest average and peak Internet speeds in the United States, with the third-highest worldwide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-184"><a href="#cite_note-184">[184]</a></sup> Northern Virginia's <a href="/wiki/Data_center" title="Data center">data centers</a> can carry up to 70% of the nation's internet traffic,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-185"><a href="#cite_note-185">[185]</a></sup> with <a href="/wiki/Loudoun_County,_Virginia" title="Loudoun County, Virginia">Loudoun County</a> alone home to as much data center space as <a href="/wiki/Northern_California" title="Northern California">northern California</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-186"><a href="#cite_note-186">[186]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-187"><a href="#cite_note-187">[187]</a></sup></p>
<p>Virginia companies received the fourth-highest amount of venture capital funding in the first half of 2011 after California, <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts" title="Massachusetts">Massachusetts</a>, and New York.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-188"><a href="#cite_note-188">[188]</a></sup> In 2009, <i><a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">Forbes</a></i> magazine named Virginia the best state in the nation for business for the fourth year in a row,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-189"><a href="#cite_note-189">[189]</a></sup> while <a href="/wiki/CNBC" title="CNBC">CNBC</a> named it the <a href="/wiki/America%27s_Top_States_For_Business" title="America's Top States For Business">top state for business</a> in 2007, 2009, and 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-190"><a href="#cite_note-190">[190]</a></sup> Additionally, in 2014 a survey of 12,000 small business owners found Virginia to be one of the most friendly states for small businesses.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-191"><a href="#cite_note-191">[191]</a></sup> Virginia has 20 <a href="/wiki/Fortune_500" title="Fortune 500">Fortune 500</a> companies, ranking the state eighth nationwide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-192"><a href="#cite_note-192">[192]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tysons_Corner" title="Tysons Corner">Tysons Corner</a> is one of the largest business districts in the nation.</p>
<p>Tourism in Virginia supported an estimated 210,000 jobs and generated $21.2 billion in 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-193"><a href="#cite_note-193">[193]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Arlington_County,_Virginia" title="Arlington County, Virginia">Arlington County</a> is the top tourist destination in the state by domestic spending, followed by <a href="/wiki/Fairfax_County,_Virginia" title="Fairfax County, Virginia">Fairfax County</a>, <a href="/wiki/Loudoun_County,_Virginia" title="Loudoun County, Virginia">Loudoun County</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Beach,_Virginia" title="Virginia Beach, Virginia">Virginia Beach</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fairfaxnarrowly_194-0"><a href="#cite_note-fairfaxnarrowly-194">[194]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Agriculture">Agriculture</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Farmers_in_Rockingham_County,_Virginia.jpg"><img alt="Two adult men in green and red baseball caps work with their hands while crouching down in a field of wide green leaves." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2848" data-file-width="4288" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Farmers_in_Rockingham_County%2C_Virginia.jpg/220px-Farmers_in_Rockingham_County%2C_Virginia.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Farmers_in_Rockingham_County%2C_Virginia.jpg/330px-Farmers_in_Rockingham_County%2C_Virginia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Farmers_in_Rockingham_County%2C_Virginia.jpg/440px-Farmers_in_Rockingham_County%2C_Virginia.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Farmers_in_Rockingham_County,_Virginia.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Rockingham_County,_Virginia" title="Rockingham County, Virginia">Rockingham County</a> is Virginia's leading county in agriculture.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlackwellCausey2005461_195-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlackwellCausey2005461-195">[195]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>As of 2007<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Virginia&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, agriculture occupied 32% of the land in Virginia and about 357,000 Virginian jobs were in agriculture, with over 47,000 farms, averaging 171 acres (0.27 sq mi; 0.69 km<sup>2</sup>), in a total farmland area of 8.1 million acres (12,656 sq mi; 32,780 km<sup>2</sup>). Though agriculture has declined significantly since 1960 when there were twice as many farms, it remains the largest single industry in Virginia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-196"><a href="#cite_note-196">[196]</a></sup> Tomatoes surpassed soy as the most profitable crop in Virginia in 2006, with peanuts and hay as other agricultural products.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-197"><a href="#cite_note-197">[197]</a></sup> Although it is no longer the primary crop, Virginia is still the fifth-largest producer of tobacco nationwide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-198"><a href="#cite_note-198">[198]</a></sup></p>
<p>Virginia is the largest producer of seafood on the <a href="/wiki/East_Coast_of_the_United_States" title="East Coast of the United States">East Coast</a>, with <a href="/wiki/Scallop" title="Scallop">scallops</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oyster" title="Oyster">oysters</a>, <a href="/wiki/Blue_crab" title="Blue crab">blue crabs</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Clam" title="Clam">clams</a> as the largest seafood harvests by value, and <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>, <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong" title="Hong Kong">Hong Kong</a> as the top export destinations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-govoyster_199-0"><a href="#cite_note-govoyster-199">[199]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-200"><a href="#cite_note-200">[200]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Eastern_oyster" title="Eastern oyster">Eastern oyster</a> harvests have increased from 23,000 bushels in 2001 to over 500,000 in 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-govoyster_199-1"><a href="#cite_note-govoyster-199">[199]</a></sup> Wineries and vineyards in the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Neck" title="Northern Neck">Northern Neck</a> and along the <a href="/wiki/Blue_Ridge_Mountains" title="Blue Ridge Mountains">Blue Ridge Mountains</a> also have begun to generate income and attract tourists.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wine_201-0"><a href="#cite_note-wine-201">[201]</a></sup> Virginia has the fifth-highest number of wineries in the nation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-202"><a href="#cite_note-202">[202]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Taxes">Taxes</span></h3>
<p>Virginia collects personal <a href="/wiki/Income_tax" title="Income tax">income tax</a> in five income brackets, ranging from 3.0% to 5.75%. The state sales and <a href="/wiki/Use_tax" title="Use tax">use tax</a> rate is 4.3%, while the tax rate on food is 1.5%. There is an additional 1% local tax, for a total of a 5.3% combined <a href="/wiki/Sales_tax" title="Sales tax">sales tax</a> on most Virginia purchases and 2.5% on most food.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-203"><a href="#cite_note-203">[203]</a></sup> Virginia's <a href="/wiki/Property_tax" title="Property tax">property tax</a> is set and collected at the local government level and varies throughout the Commonwealth. Real estate is also taxed at the local level based on 100% of fair market value. Tangible personal property also is taxed at the local level and is based on a percentage or percentages of original cost.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-204"><a href="#cite_note-204">[204]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Virginia" title="Culture of Virginia">Culture of Virginia</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Colonial_Williamsburg_ladies.jpg"><img alt="Five women dressed in long colonial style clothing sit on the stairs of tan and beige buildings talking. In front of them is a wooden wheelbarrow full of wicker baskets." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3872" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Colonial_Williamsburg_ladies.jpg/220px-Colonial_Williamsburg_ladies.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Colonial_Williamsburg_ladies.jpg/330px-Colonial_Williamsburg_ladies.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Colonial_Williamsburg_ladies.jpg/440px-Colonial_Williamsburg_ladies.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Colonial_Williamsburg_ladies.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Colonial Virginian culture, language, and style are reenacted in <a href="/wiki/Colonial_Williamsburg" title="Colonial Williamsburg">Williamsburg</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Virginia's culture was popularized and spread across America and the <a href="/wiki/Southern_United_States" title="Southern United States">South</a> by figures such as <a href="/wiki/George_Washington" title="George Washington">George Washington</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Jefferson" title="Thomas Jefferson">Thomas Jefferson</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Robert_E._Lee" title="Robert E. Lee">Robert E. Lee</a>. Their homes in Virginia represent the birthplace of America and the South.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcGraw200514_205-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcGraw200514-205">[205]</a></sup> Modern Virginia culture has many sources, and is part of the <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_the_Southern_United_States" title="Culture of the Southern United States">culture of the Southern United States</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischerKelly2000102.E2.80.93103_206-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischerKelly2000102.E2.80.93103-206">[206]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Smithsonian_Institution" title="Smithsonian Institution">Smithsonian Institution</a> divides Virginia into nine cultural regions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-207"><a href="#cite_note-207">[207]</a></sup></p>
<p>Besides the general <a href="/wiki/Cuisine_of_the_Southern_United_States" title="Cuisine of the Southern United States">cuisine of the Southern United States</a>, Virginia maintains its own particular traditions. <a href="/wiki/Virginia_wine" title="Virginia wine">Virginia wine</a> is made in many parts of the state.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wine_201-1"><a href="#cite_note-wine-201">[201]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Smithfield_ham" title="Smithfield ham">Smithfield ham</a>, sometimes called "Virginia ham", is a type of <a href="/wiki/Country_ham" title="Country ham">country ham</a> which is <a href="/wiki/Geographical_indication" title="Geographical indication">protected by state law</a>, and can only be produced in the town of <a href="/wiki/Smithfield,_Virginia" title="Smithfield, Virginia">Smithfield</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWilliamson200841_208-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWilliamson200841-208">[208]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Virginia_furniture" title="Virginia furniture">Virginia furniture</a> and architecture are typical of <a href="/wiki/American_colonial_architecture" title="American colonial architecture">American colonial architecture</a>. Thomas Jefferson and many of the state's early leaders favored the <a href="/wiki/Neoclassical_architecture" title="Neoclassical architecture">Neoclassical architecture</a> style, leading to its use for important state buildings. The <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania_Dutch" title="Pennsylvania Dutch">Pennsylvania Dutch</a> and their style can also be found in parts of the state.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dutch_134-1"><a href="#cite_note-dutch-134">[134]</a></sup></p>
<p>Literature in Virginia often deals with the state's extensive and sometimes troubled past. The works of <a href="/wiki/Pulitzer_Prize" title="Pulitzer Prize">Pulitzer Prize</a> winner <a href="/wiki/Ellen_Glasgow" title="Ellen Glasgow">Ellen Glasgow</a> often dealt with social inequalities and the role of women in her culture.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGrayRobinson200481.2C_103_209-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGrayRobinson200481.2C_103-209">[209]</a></sup> Glasgow's peer and close friend <a href="/wiki/James_Branch_Cabell" title="James Branch Cabell">James Branch Cabell</a> wrote extensively about the changing position of gentry in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Reconstruction_era_of_the_United_States" title="Reconstruction era of the United States">Reconstruction era</a>, and challenged its moral code with <i><a href="/wiki/Jurgen,_A_Comedy_of_Justice" title="Jurgen, A Comedy of Justice">Jurgen, A Comedy of Justice</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-210"><a href="#cite_note-210">[210]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/William_Styron" title="William Styron">William Styron</a> approached history in works such as <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Confessions_of_Nat_Turner_(1967)" title="The Confessions of Nat Turner (1967)">The Confessions of Nat Turner</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Sophie%27s_Choice_(novel)" title="Sophie's Choice (novel)">Sophie's Choice</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-211"><a href="#cite_note-211">[211]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Tom_Wolfe" title="Tom Wolfe">Tom Wolfe</a> has occasionally dealt with his southern heritage in bestsellers like <i><a href="/wiki/I_Am_Charlotte_Simmons" title="I Am Charlotte Simmons">I Am Charlotte Simmons</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-212"><a href="#cite_note-212">[212]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Mount_Vernon,_Virginia" title="Mount Vernon, Virginia">Mount Vernon</a> native <a href="/wiki/Matt_Bondurant" title="Matt Bondurant">Matt Bondurant</a> received critical acclaim for his <a href="/wiki/Historical_fiction" title="Historical fiction">historic novel</a> <i><a href="/wiki/The_Wettest_County_in_the_World" title="The Wettest County in the World">The Wettest County in the World</a></i> about moonshiners in <a href="/wiki/Franklin_County,_Virginia" title="Franklin County, Virginia">Franklin County</a> during <a href="/wiki/Prohibition_in_the_United_States" title="Prohibition in the United States">prohibition</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-213"><a href="#cite_note-213">[213]</a></sup> Virginia also names a <a href="/wiki/Poet_Laureate_of_Virginia" title="Poet Laureate of Virginia">state Poet Laureate</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-214"><a href="#cite_note-214">[214]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fine_and_performing_arts">Fine and performing arts</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Virginia" title="Music of Virginia">Music of Virginia</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wolf_Trap_(national_park)_meadow_pavilion.jpg"><img alt="A small, boxy, wooden stage with a trapezoidal overhang stands in the center of meadow. In the foreground is a running stream with a stone embankment." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2920" data-file-width="4386" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Wolf_Trap_%28national_park%29_meadow_pavilion.jpg/220px-Wolf_Trap_%28national_park%29_meadow_pavilion.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Wolf_Trap_%28national_park%29_meadow_pavilion.jpg/330px-Wolf_Trap_%28national_park%29_meadow_pavilion.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Wolf_Trap_%28national_park%29_meadow_pavilion.jpg/440px-Wolf_Trap_%28national_park%29_meadow_pavilion.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Wolf_Trap_(national_park)_meadow_pavilion.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Meadow Pavilion is one of the theaters at <a href="/wiki/Wolf_Trap_National_Park_for_the_Performing_Arts" title="Wolf Trap National Park for the Performing Arts">Wolf Trap National Park for the Performing Arts</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Rich in cultural heritage, Virginia however ranks near the bottom of U.S. states in terms of public spending on the arts, at nearly half of the national average.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-215"><a href="#cite_note-215">[215]</a></sup> The state government does fund some institutions, including the <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Museum_of_Fine_Arts" title="Virginia Museum of Fine Arts">Virginia Museum of Fine Arts</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Science_Museum_of_Virginia" title="Science Museum of Virginia">Science Museum of Virginia</a>. Other museums include the popular <a href="/wiki/Steven_F._Udvar-Hazy_Center" title="Steven F. Udvar-Hazy Center">Steven F. Udvar-Hazy Center</a> of the <a href="/wiki/National_Air_and_Space_Museum" title="National Air and Space Museum">National Air and Space Museum</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Chrysler_Museum_of_Art" title="Chrysler Museum of Art">Chrysler Museum of Art</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith200822.E2.80.9325_216-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith200822.E2.80.9325-216">[216]</a></sup> Besides these sites, many open-air museums are located in the Commonwealth, such as <a href="/wiki/Colonial_Williamsburg" title="Colonial Williamsburg">Colonial Williamsburg</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Frontier_Culture_Museum_of_Virginia" title="Frontier Culture Museum of Virginia">Frontier Culture Museum</a>, and various historic battlefields.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHowardBurnhamBurnham200688.2C_206.2C_292_217-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHowardBurnhamBurnham200688.2C_206.2C_292-217">[217]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Foundation_for_the_Humanities" title="Virginia Foundation for the Humanities">Virginia Foundation for the Humanities</a> works to improve the Commonwealth's civic, cultural, and intellectual life.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-218"><a href="#cite_note-218">[218]</a></sup></p>
<p>Theaters and venues in the Commonwealth are found both in the cities and suburbs. The <a href="/wiki/Harrison_Opera_House" title="Harrison Opera House">Harrison Opera House</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Norfolk,_Virginia" title="Norfolk, Virginia">Norfolk</a>, is home of the <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Opera" title="Virginia Opera">Virginia Opera</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Symphony_Orchestra" title="Virginia Symphony Orchestra">Virginia Symphony Orchestra</a> operates in and around <a href="/wiki/Hampton_Roads" title="Hampton Roads">Hampton Roads</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHowardBurnhamBurnham2006165.E2.80.93166_219-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHowardBurnhamBurnham2006165.E2.80.93166-219">[219]</a></sup> Resident and touring theater troupes operate from the <a href="/wiki/American_Shakespeare_Center" title="American Shakespeare Center">American Shakespeare Center</a> in <a href="/wiki/Staunton,_Virginia" title="Staunton, Virginia">Staunton</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGoodwin2012154_220-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGoodwin2012154-220">[220]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Barter_Theatre" title="Barter Theatre">Barter Theatre</a>, designated the State Theatre of Virginia, in <a href="/wiki/Abingdon,_Virginia" title="Abingdon, Virginia">Abingdon</a> won the first <a href="/wiki/Regional_Theatre_Tony_Award" title="Regional Theatre Tony Award">Regional Theatre Tony Award</a> in 1948, while the <a href="/wiki/Signature_Theatre_(Arlington,_Virginia)" title="Signature Theatre (Arlington, Virginia)">Signature Theatre</a> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arlington,_Virginia" title="Arlington, Virginia">Arlington</a> won it in 2009. There is also a Children's Theater of Virginia, <a href="/wiki/Theatre_IV" title="Theatre IV">Theatre IV</a>, which is the second largest touring troupe nationwide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-221"><a href="#cite_note-221">[221]</a></sup></p>
<p>Virginia has launched many award-winning traditional musical artists and internationally successful popular music acts, as well as Hollywood actors.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-factpack_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-factpack-1">[1]</a></sup> Virginia is known for its tradition in the music genres of <a href="/wiki/Old-time_music" title="Old-time music">old-time string</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bluegrass_music" title="Bluegrass music">bluegrass</a>, with groups such as the <a href="/wiki/Carter_Family" title="Carter Family">Carter Family</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stanley_Brothers" title="Stanley Brothers">Stanley Brothers</a>, as well as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gospel_(music)" title="Gospel (music)">gospel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Blues" title="Blues">blues</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Shout_band" title="Shout band">shout bands</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-222"><a href="#cite_note-222">[222]</a></sup> Contemporary Virginia is also known for <a href="/wiki/Folk_rock" title="Folk rock">folk rock</a> artists like <a href="/wiki/Dave_Matthews" title="Dave Matthews">Dave Matthews</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jason_Mraz" title="Jason Mraz">Jason Mraz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hip_hop" title="Hip hop">hip hop</a> stars like <a href="/wiki/Pharrell_Williams" title="Pharrell Williams">Pharrell Williams</a> and <a href="/wiki/Missy_Elliott" title="Missy Elliott">Missy Elliott</a>, as well as <a href="/wiki/Thrash_metal" title="Thrash metal">thrash metal</a> groups like <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/GWAR" title="GWAR">GWAR</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lamb_of_God_(band)" title="Lamb of God (band)">Lamb of God</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-223"><a href="#cite_note-223">[223]</a></sup> Notable performance venues include <a href="/wiki/The_Birchmere" title="The Birchmere">The Birchmere</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Landmark_Theater_(Richmond,_Virginia)" title="Landmark Theater (Richmond, Virginia)">Landmark Theater</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Jiffy_Lube_Live" title="Jiffy Lube Live">Jiffy Lube Live</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHowardBurnhamBurnham200629.2C_121.2C_363.2C_432_224-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHowardBurnhamBurnham200629.2C_121.2C_363.2C_432-224">[224]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Wolf_Trap_National_Park_for_the_Performing_Arts" title="Wolf Trap National Park for the Performing Arts">Wolf Trap National Park for the Performing Arts</a> is located in <a href="/wiki/Vienna,_Virginia" title="Vienna, Virginia">Vienna</a> and is the only national park intended for use as a performing arts center.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wolftrap_225-0"><a href="#cite_note-wolftrap-225">[225]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Festivals">Festivals</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Chincoteague_pony_swim_2007.jpg"><img alt="Dozens of brown and white ponies surge out of the shallow water onto a grassy shore crowded with onlookers." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2196" data-file-width="3804" height="127" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Chincoteague_pony_swim_2007.jpg/220px-Chincoteague_pony_swim_2007.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Chincoteague_pony_swim_2007.jpg/330px-Chincoteague_pony_swim_2007.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Chincoteague_pony_swim_2007.jpg/440px-Chincoteague_pony_swim_2007.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Chincoteague_pony_swim_2007.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The annual <a href="/wiki/Chincoteague_Pony" title="Chincoteague Pony">Chincoteague Pony</a> Swim features over 200 wild ponies swimming across the <a href="/wiki/Assateague_Channel" title="Assateague Channel">Assateague Channel</a> into <a href="/wiki/Chincoteague,_Virginia" title="Chincoteague, Virginia">Chincoteague</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Many counties and localities host <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/County_fair" title="County fair">county fairs</a> and festivals. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Virginia_State_Fair" title="Virginia State Fair">Virginia State Fair</a> is held at the <a href="/wiki/Meadow_Event_Park" title="Meadow Event Park">Meadow Event Park</a> every September. Also in September is the <a href="/wiki/Neptune_Festival" title="Neptune Festival">Neptune Festival</a> in <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Beach,_Virginia" title="Virginia Beach, Virginia">Virginia Beach</a>, which celebrates the city, the waterfront, and regional artists. <a href="/wiki/Norfolk,_Virginia#Parks_and_recreation" title="Norfolk, Virginia">Norfolk's Harborfest</a>, in June, features boat racing and <a href="/wiki/Air_show" title="Air show">air shows</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGoodwin201225.2C_287_226-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGoodwin201225.2C_287-226">[226]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Fairfax_County,_Virginia" title="Fairfax County, Virginia">Fairfax County</a> also sponsors <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Celebrate_Fairfax!&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Celebrate Fairfax! (page does not exist)">Celebrate Fairfax!</a> with popular and traditional music performances.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-227"><a href="#cite_note-227">[227]</a></sup> The Virginia Lake Festival is held during the third weekend in July in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Clarksville,_VA" title="Clarksville, VA">Clarksville</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-228"><a href="#cite_note-228">[228]</a></sup> Wolf Trap hosts the <a href="/wiki/Wolf_Trap_Opera_Company" title="Wolf Trap Opera Company">Wolf Trap Opera Company</a>, which produces an opera festival every summer.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wolftrap_225-1"><a href="#cite_note-wolftrap-225">[225]</a></sup> Each September, Bay Days celebrates the Chesapeake Bay as well as Hampton's 400-year history since 1610, and Isle of Wight County holds a County Fair on the second week of September as well. Both feature live music performances, and other unique events.</p>
<p>On the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Shore_of_Virginia" title="Eastern Shore of Virginia">Eastern Shore</a> island of <a href="/wiki/Chincoteague,_Virginia" title="Chincoteague, Virginia">Chincoteague</a> the annual Pony Swim &amp; Auction of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Feral" title="Feral">feral</a> <a href="/wiki/Chincoteague_Pony" title="Chincoteague Pony">Chincoteague ponies</a> at the end of July is a unique local tradition expanded into a week-long carnival. The <a href="/wiki/Shenandoah_Apple_Blossom_Festival" title="Shenandoah Apple Blossom Festival">Shenandoah Apple Blossom Festival</a> is a six-day festival held annually in <a href="/wiki/Winchester,_Virginia" title="Winchester, Virginia">Winchester</a> that includes parades and <a href="/wiki/Bluegrass_music" title="Bluegrass music">bluegrass</a> concerts. The <a href="/wiki/Old-time_music" title="Old-time music">Old Time</a> Fiddlers' Convention in <a href="/wiki/Galax,_Virginia" title="Galax, Virginia">Galax</a>, begun in 1935, is one of the oldest and largest such events worldwide. Two important film festivals, the <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Film_Festival" title="Virginia Film Festival">Virginia Film Festival</a> and the <a href="/wiki/VCU_French_Film_Festival" title="VCU French Film Festival">VCU French Film Festival</a>, are held annually in <a href="/wiki/Charlottesville,_Virginia" title="Charlottesville, Virginia">Charlottesville</a> and Richmond, respectively.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGoodwin201225.E2.80.9326_229-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGoodwin201225.E2.80.9326-229">[229]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/List_of_newspapers_in_Virginia" title="List of newspapers in Virginia">List of newspapers in Virginia</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_radio_stations_in_Virginia" title="List of radio stations in Virginia">List of radio stations in Virginia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_television_stations_in_Virginia" title="List of television stations in Virginia">List of television stations in Virginia</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:USA_Today_building.jpg"><img alt="Two geometric all glass towers connected by a central atrium stand in front of a grassy walkway and under a dark and cloudy sky" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1716" data-file-width="2916" height="129" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/USA_Today_building.jpg/220px-USA_Today_building.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/USA_Today_building.jpg/330px-USA_Today_building.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/USA_Today_building.jpg/440px-USA_Today_building.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:USA_Today_building.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<i><a href="/wiki/USA_Today" title="USA Today">USA Today</a></i>, the nation's most circulated newspaper, has its headquarters in McLean.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Hampton_Roads" title="Hampton Roads">Hampton Roads</a> area is the 45th-largest <a href="/wiki/Media_market" title="Media market">media market</a> in the United States as ranked by <a href="/wiki/Nielsen_Media_Research" title="Nielsen Media Research">Nielsen Media Research</a>, while the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Richmond-Petersburg" title="Richmond-Petersburg">Richmond-Petersburg</a> area is 57th and <a href="/wiki/Roanoke,_Virginia" title="Roanoke, Virginia">Roanoke</a>-<a href="/wiki/Lynchburg,_Virginia" title="Lynchburg, Virginia">Lynchburg</a> is 66th as of 2013<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Virginia&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-230"><a href="#cite_note-230">[230]</a></sup> Northern Virginia is part of the much larger Washington, D.C. media market.</p>
<p>There are 36 <a href="/wiki/List_of_television_stations_in_Virginia" title="List of television stations in Virginia">television stations in Virginia</a>, representing each major <a href="/wiki/List_of_United_States_over-the-air_television_networks" title="List of United States over-the-air television networks">U.S. network</a>, part of 42 stations which serve Virginia viewers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-231"><a href="#cite_note-231">[231]</a></sup> More than 720 <a href="/wiki/Federal_Communications_Commission" title="Federal Communications Commission">FCC</a>-licensed FM <a href="/wiki/Radio" title="Radio">radio</a> <a href="/wiki/List_of_radio_stations_in_Virginia" title="List of radio stations in Virginia">stations broadcast in Virginia</a>, with about 300 such AM stations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-232"><a href="#cite_note-232">[232]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-233"><a href="#cite_note-233">[233]</a></sup> The nationally available <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Public_Broadcasting_Service" title="Public Broadcasting Service">Public Broadcasting Service</a> (PBS) is headquartered in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arlington,_Virginia" title="Arlington, Virginia">Arlington</a>. Independent PBS affiliates exist throughout Virginia, and the Arlington PBS member station <a href="/wiki/WETA-TV" title="WETA-TV">WETA-TV</a> produces programs such as the <i><a href="/wiki/PBS_NewsHour" title="PBS NewsHour">PBS NewsHour</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Washington_Week" title="Washington Week">Washington Week</a></i>.</p>
<p>The most circulated <a href="/wiki/List_of_newspapers_in_Virginia" title="List of newspapers in Virginia">native newspapers in the Commonwealth</a> are <a href="/wiki/Norfolk,_Virginia" title="Norfolk, Virginia">Norfolk's</a> <i><a href="/wiki/The_Virginian-Pilot" title="The Virginian-Pilot">The Virginian-Pilot</a></i> (142,476 daily subscribers), the <i><a href="/wiki/Richmond_Times-Dispatch" title="Richmond Times-Dispatch">Richmond Times-Dispatch</a></i> (108,559), and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Roanoke_Times" title="The Roanoke Times">The Roanoke Times</a></i> (78,663), as of 2014<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Virginia&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-234"><a href="#cite_note-234">[234]</a></sup> Several <a href="/wiki/Washington,_D.C." title="Washington, D.C.">Washington, D.C.</a> papers are based in <a href="/wiki/Northern_Virginia" title="Northern Virginia">Northern Virginia</a>, such as <i><a href="/wiki/The_Washington_Examiner" title="The Washington Examiner">The Washington Examiner</a></i> and <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Politico_(newspaper)" title="Politico (newspaper)">Politico</a></i>. The paper with the nation's widest circulation, <i><a href="/wiki/USA_Today" title="USA Today">USA Today</a></i>, with 1.83 million daily subscriptions, is headquartered in <a href="/wiki/McLean,_Virginia" title="McLean, Virginia">McLean</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-235"><a href="#cite_note-235">[235]</a></sup> Besides traditional forms of media, Virginia is the home base for telecommunication companies such as <a href="/wiki/Voxant" title="Voxant">Voxant</a> and <a href="/wiki/XO_Communications" title="XO Communications">XO Communications</a>. In Northern Virginia, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Washington_Post" title="The Washington Post">The Washington Post</a></i> is the dominant newspaper, since Northern VA is located in the Washington, DC metropolitan area.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Virginia" title="Education in Virginia">Education in Virginia</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rotunda_at_University_of_Virginia.jpg"><img alt="A green statue on a brown pedestal in front of a red brick, Neoclassical dome with a large portico on the front and covered walkway on the sides.." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2288" data-file-width="3688" height="136" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Rotunda_at_University_of_Virginia.jpg/220px-Rotunda_at_University_of_Virginia.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Rotunda_at_University_of_Virginia.jpg/330px-Rotunda_at_University_of_Virginia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Rotunda_at_University_of_Virginia.jpg/440px-Rotunda_at_University_of_Virginia.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rotunda_at_University_of_Virginia.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Virginia" title="University of Virginia">University of Virginia</a>, a <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Site</a>, was founded by President <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Jefferson" title="Thomas Jefferson">Thomas Jefferson</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-236"><a href="#cite_note-236">[236]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Virginia's educational system consistently ranks in the top ten states on the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Education" title="United States Department of Education">U.S. Department of Education's</a> <a href="/wiki/National_Assessment_of_Educational_Progress" title="National Assessment of Educational Progress">National Assessment of Educational Progress</a>, with Virginia students outperforming the average in all subject areas and grade levels tested.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-237"><a href="#cite_note-237">[237]</a></sup> The 2011 <i><a href="/wiki/Education_Week#Quality_Counts" title="Education Week">Quality Counts</a></i> report ranked Virginia's K–12 education fourth best in the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-238"><a href="#cite_note-238">[238]</a></sup> All school divisions must adhere to educational standards set forth by the <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Department_of_Education" title="Virginia Department of Education">Virginia Department of Education</a>, which maintains an assessment and accreditation regime known as the <a href="/wiki/Standards_of_Learning" title="Standards of Learning">Standards of Learning</a> to ensure accountability.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-239"><a href="#cite_note-239">[239]</a></sup> In 2010, 85% of high school students graduated on-time after four years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-240"><a href="#cite_note-240">[240]</a></sup> Between 2000 and 2008, school enrollment increased 5%, the number of teachers 21%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-241"><a href="#cite_note-241">[241]</a></sup></p>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Public_school_(government_funded)" title="Public school (government funded)">Public</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/K%E2%80%9312_(education)" title="K–12 (education)">K–12 schools</a> in Virginia are generally operated by the counties and cities, and not by the state. As of 2011<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Virginia&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, a total of 1,267,063 students were enrolled in 1,873 local and regional schools in the Commonwealth, including three <a href="/wiki/Charter_school" title="Charter school">charter schools</a>, and an additional 109 alternative and special education centers across 132 <a href="/wiki/List_of_school_divisions_in_Virginia" title="List of school divisions in Virginia">school divisions</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-242"><a href="#cite_note-242">[242]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-243"><a href="#cite_note-243">[243]</a></sup> Besides the general public schools in Virginia, there are <a href="/wiki/Governor%27s_Schools_(Virginia)" title="Governor's Schools (Virginia)">Governor's Schools</a> and selective <a href="/wiki/Magnet_school" title="Magnet school">magnet schools</a>. The Governor's Schools are a collection of more than 40 regional high schools and summer programs intended for gifted students.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-244"><a href="#cite_note-244">[244]</a></sup> The Virginia Council for Private Education oversees the regulation of 320 state accredited and 130 non-accredited private schools.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-245"><a href="#cite_note-245">[245]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-246"><a href="#cite_note-246">[246]</a></sup> An additional 24,682 students receive homeschooling.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-247"><a href="#cite_note-247">[247]</a></sup></p>
<p>As of 2011<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Virginia&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, there are 176 <a href="/wiki/List_of_colleges_and_universities_in_Virginia" title="List of colleges and universities in Virginia">colleges and universities in Virginia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nces_248-0"><a href="#cite_note-nces-248">[248]</a></sup> In the 2017 <i><a href="/wiki/U.S._News_%26_World_Report" title="U.S. News &amp; World Report">U.S. News &amp; World Report</a></i> ranking of national public universities, the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Virginia" title="University of Virginia">University of Virginia</a> is ranked No. 2, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/College_of_William_and_Mary" title="College of William and Mary">College of William and Mary</a> is No. 6, <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Tech" title="Virginia Tech">Virginia Tech</a> is No. 27, <a href="/wiki/George_Mason_University" title="George Mason University">George Mason University</a> is No. 71, and <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Commonwealth_University" title="Virginia Commonwealth University">Virginia Commonwealth University</a> is No. 87.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-249"><a href="#cite_note-249">[249]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-250"><a href="#cite_note-250">[250]</a></sup> Virginia Commonwealth is also ranked the No. 1 public graduate school in fine arts, while <a href="/wiki/James_Madison_University" title="James Madison University">James Madison University</a> is ranked the No. 8 regional university in <a href="/wiki/Southern_United_States" title="Southern United States">The South</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-251"><a href="#cite_note-251">[251]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-252"><a href="#cite_note-252">[252]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Military_Institute" title="Virginia Military Institute">Virginia Military Institute</a> is the oldest state <a href="/wiki/Military_academy" title="Military academy">military college</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-253"><a href="#cite_note-253">[253]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-254"><a href="#cite_note-254">[254]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Virginia_State_University" title="Virginia State University">Virginia State University</a> and Virginia Tech are the state's <a href="/wiki/Land-grant_university" title="Land-grant university">land-grant universities</a>. Virginia also operates 23 <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Community_College_System" title="Virginia Community College System">community colleges</a> on 40 campuses serving over 260,000 students.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-255"><a href="#cite_note-255">[255]</a></sup> There are 129 private institutions in the state, including nationally ranked liberal arts colleges <a href="/wiki/Washington_and_Lee_University" title="Washington and Lee University">Washington and Lee University</a> at No. 11, the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Richmond" title="University of Richmond">University of Richmond</a> at No. 27, and the Virginia Military Institute at No. 72.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nces_248-1"><a href="#cite_note-nces-248">[248]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-256"><a href="#cite_note-256">[256]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Liberty_University" title="Liberty University">Liberty University</a> is Virginia's largest university, with an enrollment total of greater than 110,000 students.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-257"><a href="#cite_note-257">[257]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sentara_Norfolk_General.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3120" data-file-width="4160" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Sentara_Norfolk_General.jpg/220px-Sentara_Norfolk_General.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Sentara_Norfolk_General.jpg/330px-Sentara_Norfolk_General.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Sentara_Norfolk_General.jpg/440px-Sentara_Norfolk_General.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Sentara_Norfolk_General.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
