<a href="/wiki/Sentara_Norfolk_General_Hospital" title="Sentara Norfolk General Hospital">Sentara Norfolk General Hospital</a>, part of the <a href="/wiki/Hampton_Roads" title="Hampton Roads">Hampton Roads</a> based <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sentara_Health_System" title="Sentara Health System">Sentara Health System</a> and a teaching institution of <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Virginia_Medical_School" title="Eastern Virginia Medical School">Eastern Virginia Medical School</a>, was the site of the first successful <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/In-vitro_fertilization" title="In-vitro fertilization">in-vitro fertilization</a> birth.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-258"><a href="#cite_note-258">[258]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-259"><a href="#cite_note-259">[259]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Virginia has a mixed health record, and is ranked as the 26th overall healthiest state according to the 2013 United Health Foundation's Health Rankings.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ahr_260-0"><a href="#cite_note-ahr-260">[260]</a></sup> Virginia also ranks 21st among the states in the rate of premature deaths, 6,816 per 100,000. In 2008, Virginia reached its lowest ever rate of <a href="/wiki/Infant_mortality" title="Infant mortality">infant mortality</a>, at 6.7 deaths per 1,000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-261"><a href="#cite_note-261">[261]</a></sup> There are however racial and social health disparities, in 2010 African Americans experienced 28% more premature deaths than whites, while 13% of Virginians lack any <a href="/wiki/Health_insurance" title="Health insurance">health insurance</a>. According to the <a href="/wiki/Centers_for_Disease_Control_and_Prevention" title="Centers for Disease Control and Prevention">Centers for Disease Control and Prevention</a>'s 2009 survey, 26% of Virginians are obese and another 35% are overweight. 78% of residents claim to have exercised at least once in the past three months.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-262"><a href="#cite_note-262">[262]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-263"><a href="#cite_note-263">[263]</a></sup> About 30% of Virginia's 10- to 17-year-olds are overweight or obese.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-264"><a href="#cite_note-264">[264]</a></sup> Virginia banned smoking in bars and restaurants in January 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-265"><a href="#cite_note-265">[265]</a></sup> 19% of Virginians smoke tobacco.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ahr_260-1"><a href="#cite_note-ahr-260">[260]</a></sup> Residents of <a href="/wiki/Virginia%27s_8th_congressional_district" title="Virginia's 8th congressional district">Virginia's 8th congressional district</a> share the longest average <a href="/wiki/Life_expectancy" title="Life expectancy">life expectancy</a> rate in the nation, over 83 years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-266"><a href="#cite_note-266">[266]</a></sup></p>
<p>There are 89 <a href="/wiki/List_of_hospitals_in_Virginia" title="List of hospitals in Virginia">hospitals in Virginia</a> listed with the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Health_and_Human_Services" title="United States Department of Health and Human Services">United States Department of Health and Human Services</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-267"><a href="#cite_note-267">[267]</a></sup> Notable examples include <a href="/wiki/Inova_Fairfax_Hospital" title="Inova Fairfax Hospital">Inova Fairfax Hospital</a>, the largest hospital in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Washington_Metropolitan_Area" title="Washington Metropolitan Area">Washington Metropolitan Area</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/VCU_Medical_Center" title="VCU Medical Center">VCU Medical Center</a>, located on the medical campus of <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Commonwealth_University" title="Virginia Commonwealth University">Virginia Commonwealth University</a>. The University of Virginia Medical Center, part of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Virginia_Health_System" title="University of Virginia Health System">University of Virginia Health System</a>, is highly ranked in <a href="/wiki/Endocrinology" title="Endocrinology">endocrinology</a> according to <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S.News_%26_World_Report" title="U.S.News &amp; World Report">U.S.News &amp; World Report</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-268"><a href="#cite_note-268">[268]</a></sup> Virginia has a ratio of 127 <a href="/wiki/Primary_care_physician" title="Primary care physician">primary care physicians</a> per 10,000 residents, which is the 16th highest nationally.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ahr_260-2"><a href="#cite_note-ahr-260">[260]</a></sup> Virginia was one of five states to receive a perfect score in disaster preparedness according to a 2008 report by the <a href="/wiki/Trust_for_America%27s_Health" title="Trust for America's Health">Trust for America's Health</a>, based on criteria such as detecting pathogens and distributing vaccines and medical supplies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-269"><a href="#cite_note-269">[269]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">Transportation</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transportation_in_Virginia" title="Transportation in Virginia">Transportation in Virginia</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:WMATA_5000-Series_train_at_Rosslyn_station_lower_level.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1704" data-file-width="2272" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/WMATA_5000-Series_train_at_Rosslyn_station_lower_level.jpg/220px-WMATA_5000-Series_train_at_Rosslyn_station_lower_level.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/WMATA_5000-Series_train_at_Rosslyn_station_lower_level.jpg/330px-WMATA_5000-Series_train_at_Rosslyn_station_lower_level.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/WMATA_5000-Series_train_at_Rosslyn_station_lower_level.jpg/440px-WMATA_5000-Series_train_at_Rosslyn_station_lower_level.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:WMATA_5000-Series_train_at_Rosslyn_station_lower_level.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Located at the confluence of major bridges, roads, bus lines, and subway lines, <a href="/wiki/Rosslyn_station" title="Rosslyn station">Rosslyn station</a> in <a href="/wiki/Arlington_County,_Virginia" title="Arlington County, Virginia">Arlington</a> is the biggest choke point of the <a href="/wiki/Washington_Metro" title="Washington Metro">Washington Metro</a> system.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-choke1_270-0"><a href="#cite_note-choke1-270">[270]</a></sup> Arlington accounts for 40% of Virginia's public transit trips.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-271"><a href="#cite_note-271">[271]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Because of the 1932 <a href="/wiki/Byrd_Road_Act" title="Byrd Road Act">Byrd Road Act</a>, the state government controls most of Virginia's roads, instead of a local county authority as is usual in other states.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-272"><a href="#cite_note-272">[272]</a></sup> As of 2011<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Virginia&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Department_of_Transportation" title="Virginia Department of Transportation">Virginia Department of Transportation</a> owns and operates 57,867 miles (93,128 km) of the total 70,105 miles (112,823 km) of roads in the state, making it the third largest state highway system in the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vdot_273-0"><a href="#cite_note-vdot-273">[273]</a></sup> Although the Washington Metropolitan Area, which includes <a href="/wiki/Northern_Virginia" title="Northern Virginia">Northern Virginia</a>, has the second worst traffic in the nation, Virginia as a whole has the 21st-lowest congestion and the average commute time is 26.9 minutes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-274"><a href="#cite_note-274">[274]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-275"><a href="#cite_note-275">[275]</a></sup> Virginia hit <a href="/wiki/Peak_car" title="Peak car">peak car</a> usage before the year 2000, making it one of the first such states.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-276"><a href="#cite_note-276">[276]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Washington_Dulles_International_Airport_at_Dusk.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1633" data-file-width="2750" height="131" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Washington_Dulles_International_Airport_at_Dusk.jpg/220px-Washington_Dulles_International_Airport_at_Dusk.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Washington_Dulles_International_Airport_at_Dusk.jpg/330px-Washington_Dulles_International_Airport_at_Dusk.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Washington_Dulles_International_Airport_at_Dusk.jpg/440px-Washington_Dulles_International_Airport_at_Dusk.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Washington_Dulles_International_Airport_at_Dusk.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The main terminal of <a href="/wiki/Washington_Dulles_International_Airport" title="Washington Dulles International Airport">Washington Dulles International Airport</a> is one of the few surviving examples of <a href="/wiki/Googie_architecture" title="Googie architecture">Space Age architecture</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Virginia has <a href="/wiki/Amtrak" title="Amtrak">Amtrak</a> passenger rail service along several corridors, and <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Railway_Express" title="Virginia Railway Express">Virginia Railway Express</a> (VRE) maintains two commuter lines into Washington, D.C. from <a href="/wiki/Fredericksburg,_Virginia" title="Fredericksburg, Virginia">Fredericksburg</a> and <a href="/wiki/Manassas,_Virginia" title="Manassas, Virginia">Manassas</a>. VRE is one of the nation's fastest growing commuter rail services, handling nearly 20,000 passengers a day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-277"><a href="#cite_note-277">[277]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Washington_Metro" title="Washington Metro">Washington Metro</a> rapid transit system serves Northern Virginia as far west as communities along I-66 in Fairfax County, with <a href="/wiki/Silver_Line_(Washington_Metro)" title="Silver Line (Washington Metro)">expansion plans</a> to reach <a href="/wiki/Loudoun_County,_Virginia" title="Loudoun County, Virginia">Loudoun County</a> by 2017.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-278"><a href="#cite_note-278">[278]</a></sup> Major freight railroads in Virginia include <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Norfolk_Southern" title="Norfolk Southern">Norfolk Southern</a> and <a href="/wiki/CSX_Transportation" title="CSX Transportation">CSX Transportation</a>. Commuter buses include the <a href="/wiki/Fairfax_Connector" title="Fairfax Connector">Fairfax Connector</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shenandoah_Valley_Commuter_Bus" title="Shenandoah Valley Commuter Bus">Shenandoah Valley Commuter Bus</a>. The Virginia Department of Transportation operates several free ferries throughout Virginia, the most notable being the Jamestown-Scotland ferry which crosses the James River in <a href="/wiki/Surry_County,_Virginia" title="Surry County, Virginia">Surry County</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-279"><a href="#cite_note-279">[279]</a></sup></p>
<p>Virginia has five major airports: <a href="/wiki/Washington_Dulles_International_Airport" title="Washington Dulles International Airport">Washington Dulles International</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ronald_Reagan_Washington_National_Airport" title="Ronald Reagan Washington National Airport">Reagan Washington National</a> in Northern Virginia, both of which handle over 20 million passengers a year; <a href="/wiki/Richmond_International_Airport" title="Richmond International Airport">Richmond International</a>; and <a href="/wiki/Newport_News/Williamsburg_International_Airport" title="Newport News/Williamsburg International Airport">Newport News/Williamsburg International Airport</a> and <a href="/wiki/Norfolk_International_Airport" title="Norfolk International Airport">Norfolk International</a> serving the Hampton Roads area. Several other airports offer limited commercial passenger service, and sixty-six public airports serve the state's aviation needs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-280"><a href="#cite_note-280">[280]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Port_Authority" title="Virginia Port Authority">Virginia Port Authority</a>'s main seaports are those in <a href="/wiki/Hampton_Roads" title="Hampton Roads">Hampton Roads</a>, which carried 17,726,251 <a href="/wiki/Short_ton" title="Short ton">short tons</a> (16,080,984 <a href="/wiki/Tonne" title="Tonne">t</a>) of bulk cargo in 2007, the sixth most of United States ports.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-281"><a href="#cite_note-281">[281]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Shore_of_Virginia" title="Eastern Shore of Virginia">Eastern Shore of Virginia</a> is the site of <a href="/wiki/Wallops_Flight_Facility" title="Wallops Flight Facility">Wallops Flight Facility</a>, a rocket testing center owned by <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">NASA</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Mid-Atlantic_Regional_Spaceport" title="Mid-Atlantic Regional Spaceport">Mid-Atlantic Regional Spaceport</a>, a commercial spaceport.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGoodwin2012305_282-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGoodwin2012305-282">[282]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-283"><a href="#cite_note-283">[283]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Space_tourism" title="Space tourism">Space tourism</a> is also offered through <a href="/wiki/Vienna,_Virginia" title="Vienna, Virginia">Vienna</a>-based <a href="/wiki/Space_Adventures" title="Space Adventures">Space Adventures</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-284"><a href="#cite_note-284">[284]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Law_and_government">Law and government</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Virginia" title="Government of Virginia">Government of Virginia</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Va_State_Capitol.JPG"><img alt="All white Neoclassical building with pediment and six columns rises on a grassy hill with a large American elm tree in the left foreground. Two boxier, but similarly styled wings are attached at the building's rear." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1704" data-file-width="2272" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Va_State_Capitol.JPG/220px-Va_State_Capitol.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Va_State_Capitol.JPG/330px-Va_State_Capitol.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Va_State_Capitol.JPG/440px-Va_State_Capitol.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Va_State_Capitol.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Virginia_State_Capitol" title="Virginia State Capitol">Virginia State Capitol</a>, designed by <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Jefferson" title="Thomas Jefferson">Thomas Jefferson</a> and <a href="/wiki/Charles-Louis_Cl%C3%A9risseau" title="Charles-Louis Clérisseau">Charles-Louis Clérisseau</a>, is home to the <a href="/wiki/Virginia_General_Assembly" title="Virginia General Assembly">Virginia General Assembly</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In colonial Virginia, free men elected the lower house of the legislature, called the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Burgesses" title="House of Burgesses">House of Burgesses</a>, which together with the Governor's Council, made the "General Assembly". Founded in 1619, the <a href="/wiki/Virginia_General_Assembly" title="Virginia General Assembly">Virginia General Assembly</a> is still in existence as the oldest legislature in the Western Hemisphere.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-burgesses_285-0"><a href="#cite_note-burgesses-285">[285]</a></sup> In 2008, the government was ranked by the <a href="/wiki/Pew_Research_Center" title="Pew Research Center">Pew Center on the States</a> with an A− in terms of its efficiency, effectiveness, and infrastructure, tied with <a href="/wiki/Utah" title="Utah">Utah</a> and <a href="/wiki/Washington_(state)" title="Washington (state)">Washington</a>. This was the second consecutive time that Virginia received the highest grade in the nation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pew_11-1"><a href="#cite_note-pew-11">[11]</a></sup></p>
<p>Since 1971, the government has functioned under the seventh <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Virginia" title="Constitution of Virginia">Constitution of Virginia</a>, which provides for a strong legislature and a unified judicial system. Similar to the <a href="/wiki/Federal_government_of_the_United_States" title="Federal government of the United States">federal structure</a>, the government is divided in <a href="/wiki/Separation_of_powers" title="Separation of powers">three branches</a>: legislative, executive, and judicial. The legislature is the <a href="/wiki/Virginia_General_Assembly" title="Virginia General Assembly">General Assembly</a>, a bicameral body whose 100-member <a href="/wiki/Virginia_House_of_Delegates" title="Virginia House of Delegates">House of Delegates</a> and 40-member <a href="/wiki/Senate_of_Virginia" title="Senate of Virginia">Senate</a> write the laws for the Commonwealth. The Assembly is stronger than the executive, as it selects judges and justices. The Governor and <a href="/wiki/Lieutenant_Governor_of_Virginia" title="Lieutenant Governor of Virginia">Lieutenant Governor</a> are elected every four years in separate elections. Incumbent <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_Virginia_Governors" title="List of Virginia Governors">governors</a> cannot run for re-election, however the Lieutenant Governor and <a href="/wiki/Attorney_General_of_Virginia" title="Attorney General of Virginia">Attorney General</a> can, and governors may serve non-consecutive terms.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-constitution_286-0"><a href="#cite_note-constitution-286">[286]</a></sup> The judicial system, the oldest in America, consists of a hierarchy from the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_Virginia" title="Supreme Court of Virginia">Supreme Court of Virginia</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Court_of_Appeals_of_Virginia" title="Court of Appeals of Virginia">Court of Appeals of Virginia</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Circuit_Court" title="Virginia Circuit Court">Circuit Courts</a>, the trial courts of general jurisdiction, and the lower <a href="/wiki/Virginia_General_District_Court" title="Virginia General District Court">General District Courts</a> and <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Juvenile_and_Domestic_Relations_District_Court" title="Virginia Juvenile and Domestic Relations District Court">Juvenile and Domestic Relations District Courts</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-287"><a href="#cite_note-287">[287]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Code_of_Virginia" title="Code of Virginia">Code of Virginia</a> is the statutory law, and consists of the codified legislation of the General Assembly. The <a href="/wiki/Virginia_State_Police" title="Virginia State Police">Virginia State Police</a> is the largest <a href="/wiki/List_of_law_enforcement_agencies_in_Virginia" title="List of law enforcement agencies in Virginia">law enforcement agency in Virginia</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Capitol_Police" title="Virginia Capitol Police">Virginia Capitol Police</a> is the oldest police department in the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-288"><a href="#cite_note-288">[288]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Virginia_National_Guard" title="Virginia National Guard">Virginia National Guard</a> consists of 7,500 soldiers in the <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Army_National_Guard" title="Virginia Army National Guard">Virginia Army National Guard</a> and 1,200 airmen in the <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Air_National_Guard" title="Virginia Air National Guard">Virginia Air National Guard</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-289"><a href="#cite_note-289">[289]</a></sup> Since the resumption of <a href="/wiki/Capital_punishment_in_Virginia" title="Capital punishment in Virginia">capital punishment in Virginia</a> in 1982, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_individuals_executed_in_Virginia" title="List of individuals executed in Virginia">107 people have been executed</a>, the second highest number in the nation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-290"><a href="#cite_note-290">[290]</a></sup> The "total crime risk" is 28% lower than the national average.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-quick_291-0"><a href="#cite_note-quick-291">[291]</a></sup> Since Virginia ended prisoner parole in 1995, the rate of <a href="/wiki/Recidivism" title="Recidivism">recidivism</a> has fallen to 28.3%, among the lowest nationwide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-292"><a href="#cite_note-292">[292]</a></sup> Virginia is an <a href="/wiki/Open_carry_in_the_United_States" title="Open carry in the United States">open-carry state</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Virginia" title="Politics of Virginia">Politics of Virginia</a></div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_of_Virginia" title="Democratic Party of Virginia">Democratic Party of Virginia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Green_Party_of_Virginia" title="Green Party of Virginia">Green Party of Virginia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Independent_Greens_of_Virginia" title="Independent Greens of Virginia">Independent Greens of Virginia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Libertarian_Party_of_Virginia" title="Libertarian Party of Virginia">Libertarian Party of Virginia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Political_party_strength_in_Virginia" title="Political party strength in Virginia">Political party strength in Virginia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_of_Virginia" title="Republican Party of Virginia">Republican Party of Virginia</a></div>

<p>Over the 20th century, Virginia shifted from a largely rural, <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_the_Southern_United_States" title="Politics of the Southern United States">politically Southern</a> and conservative state to a more urbanized, pluralistic, and politically moderate environment. Up until the 1970s, Virginia was a racially divided <a href="/wiki/Solid_South" title="Solid South">one-party state</a> dominated by the <a href="/wiki/Byrd_Organization" title="Byrd Organization">Byrd Organization</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-294"><a href="#cite_note-294">[294]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/History_of_slavery_in_Virginia" title="History of slavery in Virginia">legacy of slavery in the state</a> effectively <a href="/wiki/Disfranchisement" title="Disfranchisement">disfranchised</a> African Americans until after passage of civil rights legislation in the mid-1960s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-295"><a href="#cite_note-295">[295]</a></sup> Enfranchisement and immigration of other groups, especially Hispanics, have placed growing importance on minority voting,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-296"><a href="#cite_note-296">[296]</a></sup> while voters that identify as "white working-class" declined by three percent between 2008 and 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-obama12_297-0"><a href="#cite_note-obama12-297">[297]</a></sup> Regional differences play a large part in Virginia politics.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-298"><a href="#cite_note-298">[298]</a></sup> Rural southern and western areas moved to support the <a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States)" title="Republican Party (United States)">Republican Party</a> in response to its "<a href="/wiki/Southern_strategy" title="Southern strategy">southern strategy</a>", while urban and growing suburban areas, including much of <a href="/wiki/Northern_Virginia" title="Northern Virginia">Northern Virginia</a>, form the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">Democratic Party</a> <a href="/wiki/Base_(politics)" title="Base (politics)">base</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-299"><a href="#cite_note-299">[299]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-300"><a href="#cite_note-300">[300]</a></sup> Democratic support also persists in union-influenced <a href="/wiki/Roanoke,_Virginia" title="Roanoke, Virginia">Roanoke</a> in <a href="/wiki/Southwest_Virginia" title="Southwest Virginia">Southwest Virginia</a>, college towns such as <a href="/wiki/Charlottesville,_Virginia" title="Charlottesville, Virginia">Charlottesville</a> and <a href="/wiki/Blacksburg,_Virginia" title="Blacksburg, Virginia">Blacksburg</a>, and the southeastern <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Black_Belt_Region" title="Black Belt Region">Black Belt Region</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-301"><a href="#cite_note-301">[301]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Political_party_strength_in_Virginia" title="Political party strength in Virginia">Political party strength in Virginia</a> has likewise been in flux. In the <a href="/wiki/Virginia_state_elections,_2007" title="Virginia state elections, 2007">2007 state elections</a>, Democrats regained control of the <a href="/wiki/Senate_of_Virginia" title="Senate of Virginia">State Senate</a>, and narrowed the Republican majority in the <a href="/wiki/Virginia_House_of_Delegates" title="Virginia House of Delegates">House of Delegates</a> to eight seats.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-302"><a href="#cite_note-302">[302]</a></sup> Yet <a href="/wiki/Virginia_elections,_2009" title="Virginia elections, 2009">elections in 2009</a> resulted in the election of Republican <a href="/wiki/Bob_McDonnell" title="Bob McDonnell">Bob McDonnell</a> as <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_Virginia" title="Governor of Virginia">Governor</a> by a seventeen-point margin, the election of a Republican <a href="/wiki/Lieutenant_Governor_of_Virginia" title="Lieutenant Governor of Virginia">Lieutenant Governor</a> and <a href="/wiki/Attorney_General_of_Virginia" title="Attorney General of Virginia">Attorney General</a>, as well as Republican gains of six seats in the House of Delegates.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-303"><a href="#cite_note-303">[303]</a></sup> In 2011, the Republican caucus took over two-thirds (68–32) of the seats in the House of Delegates, and a majority of the Senate based on the Lieutenant Governor <a href="/wiki/Bill_Bolling" title="Bill Bolling">Bill Bolling</a> as the tie-breaker.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-304"><a href="#cite_note-304">[304]</a></sup> Following the <a href="/wiki/Virginia_elections,_2013" title="Virginia elections, 2013">2013 elections</a>, Democrat <a href="/wiki/Terry_McAuliffe" title="Terry McAuliffe">Terry McAuliffe</a> was elected Governor by two percentage points,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-305"><a href="#cite_note-305">[305]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-306"><a href="#cite_note-306">[306]</a></sup> and Democrat <a href="/wiki/Ralph_Northam" title="Ralph Northam">Ralph Northam</a> was elected Lieutenant Governor by double digits.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-elections.huffingtonpost.com_307-0"><a href="#cite_note-elections.huffingtonpost.com-307">[307]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-308"><a href="#cite_note-308">[308]</a></sup> Republicans, however, maintained their super-majority (68–32) in the House of Delegates.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-elections.huffingtonpost.com_307-1"><a href="#cite_note-elections.huffingtonpost.com-307">[307]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-309"><a href="#cite_note-309">[309]</a></sup> State election seasons traditionally start with the annual <a href="/wiki/Shad_Planking" title="Shad Planking">Shad Planking</a> event in <a href="/wiki/Wakefield,_Virginia" title="Wakefield, Virginia">Wakefield</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-310"><a href="#cite_note-310">[310]</a></sup></p>
<p>In federal elections since 2006, both parties have seen successes. Republican Senator <a href="/wiki/George_Allen_(U.S._politician)" title="George Allen (U.S. politician)">George Allen</a> lost close races in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Virginia_United_States_Senate_election,_2006" title="Virginia United States Senate election, 2006">2006</a>, to Democratic newcomer <a href="/wiki/Jim_Webb" title="Jim Webb">Jim Webb</a>, and again in <a href="/wiki/United_States_Senate_election_in_Virginia,_2012" title="United States Senate election in Virginia, 2012">2012</a>, to Webb's replacement, former Governor <a href="/wiki/Tim_Kaine" title="Tim Kaine">Tim Kaine</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-311"><a href="#cite_note-311">[311]</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/United_States_Senate_election_in_Virginia,_2008" title="United States Senate election in Virginia, 2008">2008</a>, Democrats won both <a href="/wiki/United_States_Senate" title="United States Senate">United States Senate</a> seats; former Governor <a href="/wiki/Mark_Warner" title="Mark Warner">Mark Warner</a> was elected to replace retiring Republican <a href="/wiki/John_Warner" title="John Warner">John Warner</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-312"><a href="#cite_note-312">[312]</a></sup> The state went Republican in 13 out of 14 <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election" title="United States presidential election">presidential elections</a> from 1952 to 2004, including 10 in a row from 1968 to 2004. However, Democrat <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> carried Virginia's 13 <a href="/wiki/Electoral_College_(United_States)" title="Electoral College (United States)">electoral votes</a> in both the <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_2008" title="United States presidential election, 2008">2008</a> and <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_2012" title="United States presidential election, 2012">2012</a> presidential elections.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-obama12_297-1"><a href="#cite_note-obama12-297">[297]</a></sup> In the <a href="/wiki/Virginia_elections,_2010" title="Virginia elections, 2010">2010 elections</a>, Republicans won three <a href="/wiki/United_States_House_of_Representatives" title="United States House of Representatives">United States House of Representatives</a> seats from the Democrats. Of the state's <a href="/wiki/List_of_United_States_Representatives_from_Virginia" title="List of United States Representatives from Virginia">eleven seats</a> in the House of Representatives, Republicans hold seven and Democrats hold four. Virginia is considered a "<a href="/wiki/Swing_state" title="Swing state">swing state</a>" in future presidential elections.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-purple_9-1"><a href="#cite_note-purple-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the 2016 Presidential election, Democrat <a href="/wiki/Hillary_Clinton" title="Hillary Clinton">Hillary Clinton</a> carried Virginia, marking the third consecutive win for the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">Democratic Party</a> at the presidential level and the first time the state gave its electoral votes to a Democrat, who did not win the national Electoral Vote, <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election_in_Virginia,_1924" title="United States presidential election in Virginia, 1924">since 1924</a>. In contrast, the state gave <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Donald_J._Trump" title="Donald J. Trump">Donald J. Trump</a> the smallest percentage of Virginian votes for any <a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States)" title="Republican Party (United States)">Republican Party</a> presidential nominee since <a href="/wiki/Thomas_E._Dewey" title="Thomas E. Dewey">Thomas E. Dewey</a> <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election_in_Virginia,_1948" title="United States presidential election in Virginia, 1948">in 1948</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Sports_teams_in_Virginia" title="Sports teams in Virginia">Sports teams in Virginia</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Greg_Stroman_at_the_2014_Military_Bowl.jpg"><img alt="A receiver dressed in white with maroon and orange stripes is tackled by an opposing player in black and red." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1800" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Greg_Stroman_at_the_2014_Military_Bowl.jpg/220px-Greg_Stroman_at_the_2014_Military_Bowl.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Greg_Stroman_at_the_2014_Military_Bowl.jpg/330px-Greg_Stroman_at_the_2014_Military_Bowl.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Greg_Stroman_at_the_2014_Military_Bowl.jpg/440px-Greg_Stroman_at_the_2014_Military_Bowl.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Greg_Stroman_at_the_2014_Military_Bowl.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Tech_Hokies_football" title="Virginia Tech Hokies football">Virginia Tech Hokies football</a> team has the second-longest <a href="/wiki/List_of_Virginia_Tech_Hokies_bowl_games" title="List of Virginia Tech Hokies bowl games">bowl game streak</a> in the nation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-313"><a href="#cite_note-313">[313]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Virginia is the most populous U.S. state without a <a href="/wiki/Major_professional_sports_leagues_in_the_United_States_and_Canada" title="Major professional sports leagues in the United States and Canada">major professional sports league</a> franchise.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-314"><a href="#cite_note-314">[314]</a></sup> The reasons for this include the lack of any dominant city or market within the state, the proximity of <a href="/wiki/Sports_in_Washington,_D.C." title="Sports in Washington, D.C.">teams in Washington, D.C.</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sports_in_North_Carolina" title="Sports in North Carolina">North Carolina</a>, and a reluctance to publicly finance stadiums.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-315"><a href="#cite_note-315">[315]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-316"><a href="#cite_note-316">[316]</a></sup> However, in recent years, the city of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Virginia_Beach" title="Virginia Beach">Virginia Beach</a> has proposed <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Beach_Arena" title="Virginia Beach Arena">a new arena</a> designed to lure a major league franchise. <a href="/wiki/Norfolk,_Virginia" title="Norfolk, Virginia">Norfolk</a> is host to two minor league teams: The <a href="/wiki/Triple-A_(baseball)" title="Triple-A (baseball)">AAA</a> <a href="/wiki/Norfolk_Tides" title="Norfolk Tides">Norfolk Tides</a> and the <a href="/wiki/ECHL" title="ECHL">ECHL</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Norfolk_Admirals_(ECHL)" title="Norfolk Admirals (ECHL)">Norfolk Admirals</a>. The <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Giants" title="San Francisco Giants">San Francisco Giants</a>' <a href="/wiki/Double-A_(baseball)" title="Double-A (baseball)">AA team</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Richmond_Flying_Squirrels" title="Richmond Flying Squirrels">Richmond Flying Squirrels</a>, began play at <a href="/wiki/The_Diamond_(Richmond,_Virginia)" title="The Diamond (Richmond, Virginia)">The Diamond</a> in 2010, replacing the AAA <a href="/wiki/Richmond_Braves" title="Richmond Braves">Richmond Braves</a>, who relocated after 2008.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-317"><a href="#cite_note-317">[317]</a></sup> Additionally, the <a href="/wiki/Washington_Nationals" title="Washington Nationals">Washington Nationals</a>, <a href="/wiki/Boston_Red_Sox" title="Boston Red Sox">Boston Red Sox</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cleveland_Indians" title="Cleveland Indians">Cleveland Indians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Atlanta_Braves" title="Atlanta Braves">Atlanta Braves</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Pirates" title="Pittsburgh Pirates">Pittsburgh Pirates</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_York_Yankees" title="New York Yankees">New York Yankees</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Toronto_Blue_Jays" title="Toronto Blue Jays">Toronto Blue Jays</a> also have Single-A and Rookie-level <a href="/wiki/Farm_team" title="Farm team">farm teams</a> in Virginia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-318"><a href="#cite_note-318">[318]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Washington_Redskins" title="Washington Redskins">Washington Redskins</a> have Redskins Park, their headquarters, in <a href="/wiki/Ashburn,_Virginia" title="Ashburn, Virginia">Ashburn</a> and their training facility is in Richmond,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-319"><a href="#cite_note-319">[319]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Washington_Capitals" title="Washington Capitals">Washington Capitals</a> train at <a href="/wiki/Kettler_Capitals_Iceplex" title="Kettler Capitals Iceplex">Kettler Capitals Iceplex</a> in <a href="/wiki/Ballston,_Arlington,_Virginia" title="Ballston, Arlington, Virginia">Ballston</a>. Virginia has many professional caliber golf courses including the <a href="/wiki/Greg_Norman" title="Greg Norman">Greg Norman</a> course at Lansdowne Resort and Kingsmill Resort, home of the <a href="/wiki/Kingsmill_Championship" title="Kingsmill Championship">Kingsmill Championship</a>, an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/LPGA_Tour" title="LPGA Tour">LPGA Tour</a> tournament. <a href="/wiki/NASCAR" title="NASCAR">NASCAR</a> currently schedules <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sprint_Cup_Series" title="Sprint Cup Series">Sprint Cup</a> races on two tracks in Virginia: <a href="/wiki/Martinsville_Speedway" title="Martinsville Speedway">Martinsville Speedway</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Richmond_International_Raceway" title="Richmond International Raceway">Richmond International Raceway</a>. Virginia natives currently competing in the series include <a href="/wiki/Denny_Hamlin" title="Denny Hamlin">Denny Hamlin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Elliott_Sadler" title="Elliott Sadler">Elliott Sadler</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-320"><a href="#cite_note-320">[320]</a></sup></p>
<p>Virginia does not allow state appropriated funds to be used for either operational or capital expenses for intercollegiate athletics.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-321"><a href="#cite_note-321">[321]</a></sup> Despite this, both the <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Cavaliers" title="Virginia Cavaliers">Virginia Cavaliers</a> and <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Tech_Hokies" title="Virginia Tech Hokies">Virginia Tech Hokies</a> have been able to field competitive teams in the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Coast_Conference" title="Atlantic Coast Conference">Atlantic Coast Conference</a> and maintain modern facilities. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Virginia-Virginia_Tech_rivalry" title="Virginia-Virginia Tech rivalry">Their rivalry</a> is followed statewide. <a href="/wiki/List_of_college_athletic_programs_in_Virginia" title="List of college athletic programs in Virginia">Twelve other universities</a> compete in <a href="/wiki/National_Collegiate_Athletic_Association" title="National Collegiate Athletic Association">NCAA</a> <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Division_I" title="NCAA Division I">Division I</a>, particularly in the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_10_Conference" title="Atlantic 10 Conference">Atlantic 10 Conference</a>, <a href="/wiki/Big_South_Conference" title="Big South Conference">Big South Conference</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Colonial_Athletic_Association" title="Colonial Athletic Association">Colonial Athletic Association</a>. Three <a href="/wiki/Historically_black_colleges_and_universities" title="Historically black colleges and universities">historically black schools</a> compete in the Division II <a href="/wiki/Central_Intercollegiate_Athletic_Association" title="Central Intercollegiate Athletic Association">Central Intercollegiate Athletic Association</a>, and two others compete in the Division I <a href="/wiki/Mid-Eastern_Athletic_Conference" title="Mid-Eastern Athletic Conference">Mid-Eastern Athletic Conference</a>. Several smaller schools compete in the <a href="/wiki/Old_Dominion_Athletic_Conference" title="Old Dominion Athletic Conference">Old Dominion Athletic Conference</a> and the <a href="/wiki/USA_South_Athletic_Conference" title="USA South Athletic Conference">USA South Athletic Conference</a> of NCAA Division III. The NCAA currently holds its <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Division_III_(NCAA)" title="Division III (NCAA)">Division III</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NCAA_Division_III_national_football_championship" title="NCAA Division III national football championship">championships in football</a>, men's basketball, volleyball and softball in <a href="/wiki/Salem,_Virginia" title="Salem, Virginia">Salem</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-322"><a href="#cite_note-322">[322]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="State_symbols">State symbols</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Virginia_state_symbols" title="List of Virginia state symbols">List of Virginia state symbols</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Welcome_to_Virginia_Sign.jpg"><img alt='A large rectangular metal sign, mostly black, with the words "Welcome To Virginia" and "Virginia is for lovers" with a red heart symbol on the left.' class="thumbimage" data-file-height="225" data-file-width="350" height="141" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Welcome_to_Virginia_Sign.jpg/220px-Welcome_to_Virginia_Sign.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Welcome_to_Virginia_Sign.jpg/330px-Welcome_to_Virginia_Sign.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/1/10/Welcome_to_Virginia_Sign.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Welcome_to_Virginia_Sign.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The state slogan, "<a href="/wiki/Virginia_is_for_Lovers" title="Virginia is for Lovers">Virginia is for Lovers</a>," was developed in 1968 and is featured on the state's welcome signs</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The state nickname is its oldest symbol, though it has never been made official by law. Virginia was given the title "<a href="/wiki/Dominion" title="Dominion">Dominion</a>" by King <a href="/wiki/Charles_II_of_England" title="Charles II of England">Charles II of England</a> at the time of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Restoration" title="The Restoration">The Restoration</a>, because it had remained loyal to the crown during the <a href="/wiki/English_Civil_War" title="English Civil War">English Civil War</a>, and the present moniker, "Old Dominion" is a reference to that title. Charles' supporters were called <a href="/wiki/Cavalier" title="Cavalier">Cavaliers</a>, and "The Cavalier State" nickname was popularized after the <a href="/wiki/American_Civil_War" title="American Civil War">American Civil War</a> to romanticize the antebellum period. Sports teams from the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Virginia" title="University of Virginia">University of Virginia</a> are called the <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Cavaliers" title="Virginia Cavaliers">Cavaliers</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWelch20061.E2.80.933_323-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWelch20061.E2.80.933-323">[323]</a></sup> The other nickname, "Mother of Presidents", is also historic, as eight Virginians have served as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lists_of_United_States_Presidents_by_place_of_birth#By_state_of_birth" title="Lists of United States Presidents by place of birth">President of the United States</a>, including four of the first five.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-factpack_1-2"><a href="#cite_note-factpack-1">[1]</a></sup></p>
<p>The state's motto, <i><a href="/wiki/Sic_semper_tyrannis" title="Sic semper tyrannis">Sic Semper Tyrannis</a></i>, translates from Latin as "Thus Always to Tyrants", and is used on the state seal, which is then used on the flag. While the seal was designed in 1776, and the flag was first used in the 1830s, both were made official in 1930.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-factpack_1-3"><a href="#cite_note-factpack-1">[1]</a></sup> The majority of the other symbols were made official in the late 20th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-324"><a href="#cite_note-324">[324]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Virginia_reel_(dance)" title="Virginia reel (dance)">Virginia reel</a> is among the <a href="/wiki/Square_dance" title="Square dance">square dances</a> classified as the <a href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._state_dances" title="List of U.S. state dances">state dance</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-eov_12-1"><a href="#cite_note-eov-12">[12]</a></sup> In March 2015, after 20 years without a <a href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._state_songs" title="List of U.S. state songs">state song</a>, Virginia received two: "<a href="/wiki/Our_Great_Virginia" title="Our Great Virginia">Our Great Virginia</a>" (official traditional state song) and "<a href="/wiki/Sweet_Virginia_Breeze" title="Sweet Virginia Breeze">Sweet Virginia Breeze</a>" (official popular state song).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-325"><a href="#cite_note-325">[325]</a></sup> In 1940, Virginia made "<a href="/wiki/Carry_Me_Back_to_Old_Virginny" title="Carry Me Back to Old Virginny">Carry Me Back to Old Virginny</a>" the state song, but it was retired in 1997 and reclassified as the state song emeritus.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-326"><a href="#cite_note-326">[326]</a></sup></p>
